The next operational chapter places the subject on the active roster of the Avengers under Jason Aaron's stewardship, in the context of the unleashed Prehistoric Avengers / Final Host / Starbrand storylines. The recruitment is structurally interesting: he is not asked because he is a team player but because the team has assessed that the threat-class involved (cosmic-tier, ancient, theological) requires someone who can be deployed against Heaven-adjacent and demon-adjacent targets with no political constraint.

The subject's tenure is characterized by a small number of stable behavioral facts:

- **Quartering.** He selects the Avengers Mountain sub-levels for his personal quarters, descending several floors below the operational levels. He does not decorate. He does not request furnishings. The space contains a cot, a footlocker, and the bike. He treats it as a garage with a bed in it.
- **Mealtime absence.** He does not appear at communal meals. When required for briefings, he stands at the rear of the room, declines seating, and leaves before incidental conversation begins. This is observed across multiple incidents and is consistent enough to qualify as a rule.
- **Mission discipline.** In the field, he is tactically excellent, terse on comms, and notably tolerant of the team's more grandiose members in a way that suggests practiced non-engagement rather than affection. He follows Captain America's calls without demur; he ignores T'Challa's strategic refinements without comment and executes them anyway; he treats Thor with a guarded, peer-level wariness rooted in their respective theological grievances. His relationship with the female Thor / Jane Foster, when they overlap, is the warmest he allows himself on the team, and is built on a shared recognition of bodies-used-up-by-a-mantle.
- **Refusal of leadership.** When tactical leadership of sub-teams is delegated, he declines or accepts and immediately ratifies the next available alternative. He will not be in charge.
- **Compliance without integration.** He attends required functions. He does not attend optional ones. He does not socialize. He does not drink with teammates; he drinks alone, in the bunk, after.

The most diagnostically revealing episode of the tenure is the Starbrand-child arc — the recovery of an infant carrying the Starbrand power. The subject's behavior shifts visibly. He is the first to volunteer for guardianship. He physically interposes himself between the child and threats with no audible tactical calculus. He speaks to the infant directly, in tones not previously observed in his vocal record on the team. When the child is removed from his immediate care by team decision, he absents himself for approximately seventy-two hours and returns without explanation.

The Starbrand episode confirms what the rest of the tenure suggests: he is on the team in body. He is, internally, present only when a child enters the operational frame. Then he is incandescent.

---

## 4. The Brisson Relaunch: The False Suburb and the Bone Hunters

The Brisson-era solo material catches the subject in a brief, fragile, and ultimately fraudulent period of attempted reintegration. The narrative substrate — the subject has been, by some agency, granted what reads as a normal life, a wife, a home, suburban stability — is revealed across the arc to be a constructed delusion or otherworldly trap. The behavioral data this generates is invaluable because it tells us what his unconscious produces when allowed to author a life.

The constructed life contains, in approximate order of psychological weight:
- A wife (the Roxanne template, modified). His unconscious does not invent a new partner; it returns to her.
- A house, modest, not lavish. He does not fantasize wealth.
- Children. He fantasizes children, plural.
- A garage. He keeps the bike. Even in fantasy, the bike persists.
- An ordinary job, blue-collar. He does not fantasize career achievement.
- Quiet evenings. He fantasizes the absence of obligation, not the presence of pleasure.

The fantasy is, in clinical terms, almost painfully modest. It is what a working-class man who lost his childhood to a carnival might want at fifty: a wife who stays, children who grow, a garage to retreat to, and night that ends in sleep rather than transformation. When the fantasy collapses — and it always does, because the arc structures it to collapse — the subject's reaction is not rage but something closer to a flat, exhausted acceptance: he knew this was not real because nothing of the kind is permitted to him.

The arc deposits him back on the road by its end, accompanied for a stretch by Daniel Ketch (the brother-rivalry now operating in a more reconciled register, both men older, both worn), engaged in what amounts to a hunting/cleanup operation against entities — colloquially the "Bone Hunters" in the file shorthand — that prey on Spirit-of-Vengeance bearers. The subject is, for the first time in years, not running from the curse but running *toward* the people who hurt other curse-bearers. This is a meaningful prosocial shift: the protection-of-the-helpless drive has, finally, generalized to include people in his own structural category. He no longer treats himself as outside the class of those worth defending. He treats other bearers as worth defending, which is closer than he has come in decades to admitting he might be also.

---

## 5. The Percy Era: The Asylum, the Cracked Frame, and the Question of What Is Real

The most recent solo material (the Percy run and its successors) places the subject in a sustained narrative interrogation of the reliability of his own experience. He is, at the opening, institutionalized — committed, medicated, told that the Ghost Rider was always a delusion, that his life on the road was a fugue, that the carnival, the bargain, Roxanne, the throne, all of it is the elaborate confabulation of an unwell man.

The behavioral data the arc generates is unusually rich because it stresses the subject's reality-testing under conditions a normal stress test cannot replicate.

The subject:
- Does not collapse. He absorbs the institutional framing with the constricted, watchful affect that is his baseline.
- Tests the framing. He does not flatly reject it. He probes — checking, in small ways, whether the room behaves as a real room should, whether the orderlies are who they claim to be, whether the medication has the body-effects it should have.
- Maintains moral function inside the institution. Even in the asylum, he intervenes on behalf of fellow patients abused by staff. The drive does not require that he know himself to be Ghost Rider; it requires only that he see a smaller person being hurt by a larger one.
- Escapes when the evidence converges. He does not escape on faith. He escapes when the cumulative anomalies — too many, too patterned — exceed the threshold his concrete cognitive style requires.

The arc that follows places him on a road trip with unusually high cosmological stakes, in a register that returns him to the elemental Friedrich/Ploog template: a man, a bike, a country full of evil, the night. He is older in it. The artwork and dialogue both register a subject who has stopped expecting relief and started, with no fanfare, building a working relationship with the fact of his own continuing existence. He is not happy. He is not, any longer, actively seeking termination. This is a meaningful, if small, movement.

---

## 6. Granular Behavioral Profile, Present Day

The following are the operational facts of the subject's current existence, reconstructed from the canon and consistent across recent appearances.

**Geography.** Itinerant, U.S.-domestic. Preferred corridors: the I-40 / Route 66 ghost-corridor, the I-10 southern band, the secondary highways of New Mexico, west Texas, Arizona, Nevada, and the Mississippi Delta. Avoids: the Eastern Seaboard cities, Las Vegas (post-*Damnation* aversion), the Pacific Northwest (no recorded affinity). Pattern: nights in motion, days in single-occupancy lodging or in the bike's shadow.

**Lodging.** Independent motels, cash preferred. Single night the modal stay; two nights when the bike requires service or a wound requires it. He has not signed a lease in the operational memory of this file.

**Vehicle.** Hellcycle in its mystical aspect; in mundane form, a heavily modified Harley FXR-class frame, black, no chrome, no insignia, registration plates rotated. Maintenance performed by the subject personally. He has refused offers of upgraded transportation from multiple parties (Stark, Strange, Wakandan technical staff during the Avengers tenure). The bike is not a tool; it is a member of a household of two.

**Dress.** Black leather jacket, worn and re-repaired rather than replaced; denim; engineer boots; t-shirts in dark solids; occasionally a flannel overshirt in cold weather. No watches. No jewelry. A single wallet, a single knife, occasional concealed firearm of unremarkable caliber. The hellfire shotgun appears intermittently; he does not carry it openly.

**Eating.** Diner-pattern. Black coffee, eggs, hash, pancakes in stacks. Eats fast. Tips well in cash. Sits with line-of-sight to entrance.

**Drinking.** Continues. Beer in cans, whiskey neat, alone, late, in the room rather than at the bar when possible. The functional alcohol use disorder noted in the medical workup is not in remission; it is, however, contained — he does not appear to drink before riding, and his nightly intake is the anesthetic minimum rather than the obliterating maximum.

**Sleep.** Improved, marginally, from prior eras. Still poor. Nightmares persist. He sleeps with the curtains drawn and a chair against the door — a tradecraft habit he has had so long it is no longer conscious.

**Communications.** Burner phones, rotated. He maintains a small list of numbers he will answer: Strange, Ketch, a handful of priests across the country whose discretion he has tested, two or three motel proprietors who will hold a message. He does not carry a smartphone in any sustained way. He does not have social-media presence; the file is confident this is by character rather than by tradecraft.

**Companions.** None permanent. Periodic alliances with Ketch, with Reyes (mentor-distance), with Strange (operational), with Jane Foster when their paths cross (warm), with Wade Wilson under duress (he tolerates Wilson the way a tired man tolerates a barking dog). He has not been observed in a sustained romantic relationship in the recent era. Roxanne's status fluctuates by writer; in his internal world, she is the absent reference point regardless.

**The Rider, integration status.** Improved from the Bronze Age fugue-pattern; not complete. He retains memory of transformations. He continues to use third-person framing for the Spirit in conversation. He has, in recent material, occasionally used first-person plural ("we") — a small but meaningful linguistic concession. He is not integrated. He is in negotiated cohabitation.

**Theological posture.** Hardened. Post-Zadkiel, post-Mephisto, post-throne, he treats every entity claiming divine or infernal authority as presumptively lying. He has not entered a church for worship in the operational memory; he has entered churches for tactical purposes (consecrated ground, priest as informant, sanctuary for a victim). He prays, when he prays, in the form of brief, profane, addressed-to-no-one-in-particular monologues delivered aloud while riding.

**Moral function.** Intact. The protection-of-children drive is, if anything, more pronounced in the recent era than in any prior. He has been observed altering routes by hundreds of miles in response to a single news item about a missing child. He does not advertise these interventions; he conducts them and leaves.

**Affect.** Flattened further from baseline. The melancholic constriction noted in the psychological workup has, with age, settled into something closer to equanimity-at-the-floor — he is not depressed in an acute sense any longer so much as he is permanently quieted. The explosive-rage register remains available and is deployed in transformation. The mid-register absence — joy, playfulness — persists, with one exception: he is, on rare occasions, observed smiling at small children, briefly, in a manner inconsistent with his other affective output. The smile does not survive their parents' arrival.

---

## 7. How He Got Here

The trajectory from the Bronze Age suicide-adjacent fugitive to the present quiet ascetic is not a redemption arc. It is an attrition arc. The subject has not been healed; he has been worn smooth. Every catastrophe of the intervening decades — the Zadkiel betrayal, the loss of the Aaron-era family, the throne, the suburban fantasy, the asylum — has subtracted from his expectation of relief without subtracting from his capacity to act on behalf of others.

What remains, at the present moment, is a man who has accepted three things he formerly resisted:

1. **He will not be released from the curse.** He has stopped seeking exorcism. He has stopped seeking theological argument for separation. The bond is a fact, like weather.
2. **He will not have a private life.** The Brisson-era fantasy was the last sustained gesture toward one, and its collapse was absorbed without protest. He no longer projects forward into a domestic future.
3. **He is the one who does this work.** Not chosen, not damned-into-it, not conscripted — *the one who does it*. The agency framing is new in the recent era and is the closest the subject has come, in fifty years of recorded existence, to claiming authorship of his own life.

He has not forgiven himself. He has not concluded that he is good. He has, however, stopped requiring a verdict in order to continue.

---

## 8. Current Operational Status

**Location, present:** Unfixed. Last credible sighting consistent with the I-40 corridor, eastbound, in the past operational window. The file expects relocation within seventy-two hours of any sighting and does not maintain pin-accurate placement.

**Affiliations, current:** None formal. Loose, on-call relationships with Strange, Ketch, and a small ecclesiastical network. No active Avengers status; the tenure is concluded by mutual non-renewal rather than by rupture.

**Threat posture, to civilian populations:** Net protective. The subject's collateral-damage record is unusually clean for an actor at his power tier; he is meticulous about non-combatant safety in a way that reflects the carnival-era training (a stunt rider learns where the crowd is) more than any superhero doctrine.

**Threat posture, to peer actors:** Conditional. He is non-aggressive toward any party not actively predating on the vulnerable. He is implacable toward parties that are. The Penance Stare remains his terminal-tier instrument and is deployed, in the recent era, with the practiced discrimination of a man who has had decades to consider its weight.

**Recruitability:** Low. He can be asked, once, by an actor he respects, for a specific intervention with a specific moral stake. He cannot be retained.

**Prognosis:** Stable in the depressive-functional register. No acute crisis indicated. No active suicidal behavior, though the long-running passive accommodation persists. Improvement, where it exists, is incremental and may not be visible to the subject. He will continue, in the file's assessment, to ride, to intervene, to drink alone, to sleep poorly, and to refuse the verdict on himself that his behavior has, for fifty years, been quietly earning.

He is, at present, the most stable he has ever been. This is not the same as well. It is, however, the condition in which he is most likely to continue, and the file assesses that continuation — for him, for the people he intercepts on the road, for the children he diverts hundreds of miles to find — is the operative good.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — SUBJECT: JOHN "JOHNNY" BLAZE

*Compiled from longitudinal canonical record, 1972–present. Pre-curse history reconstructed from carnival-era flashbacks (Friedrich, Mantlo, Aaron retrospectives); post-curse from continuous observational record across six decades of incident reporting.*

---

## I. CONSTITUTIONAL BASELINE

**Anthropometrics, adult.** Caucasian male, approximately 5'11" / 180 cm, 175–185 lb depending on era, athletic-lean ectomesomorph with the specific musculature distribution one sees in lifelong motorcyclists: pronounced forearm flexor development from grip-loading; well-developed lateral and posterior deltoids from countersteering and tank-grip stabilization; iliopsoas and adductor tone from saddle-clenching; cervical paraspinals overdeveloped from helmeted high-speed head-stabilization. Resting heart rate, where canonically depictable, runs low — consistent with sustained cardiovascular conditioning that pre-dates any supernatural alteration.

**Skin.** Pre-curse: weather-cured, sun-damaged on the dorsal hands, forearms, posterior neck, and lower face below the eye-line where helmet visors terminate. Wind-tan asymmetric along the left cheek (prevailing-wind exposure from sustained westward riding). Multiple healed road-rash scars across right hip, left shoulder, both knees, and the dorsal aspect of the left forearm — the carnival circuit produced these by the time he was nineteen. Post-curse: skin condition is *intermittently moot*, as it is consumed and reconstituted with each transformation; over time, however, observers note that the reconstituted flesh has lost certain old scars and acquired a faintly ageless quality. He looks roughly his Bronze Age age across decades. This is not a benefit he has welcomed.

**Dentition.** Originally unremarkable; two anterior teeth chipped in a 1970s wreck, never restored cosmetically. The transformation regrows them each cycle in their pre-trauma configuration, which Blaze finds, by his own muttering, "wrong." He has been observed running his tongue across his upper incisors in idle moments — a tell, present from the late 1970s forward, of someone checking whether his body is still his.

**Vision and hearing.** 20/20 or better corrected; no eyewear. Hearing shows the high-frequency attenuation expected of a man who has spent forty years inside open-pipe exhaust at sustained RPM without consistent ear protection — he sometimes asks for things to be repeated in noisy rooms and orients his right ear (the dominant) toward speakers in low-light environments.

---

## II. PRE-CURSE INJURY LEDGER (CARNIVAL ERA, c. AGES 12–22)

The Crash Simpson Stunt Cycle Show was the medical antechamber to everything that followed. Boys learning to ride ramps and through fire absorb injuries the way apprentice carpenters absorb splinters — chronically, undocumented, and as a condition of continued employment.

**Fractures, healed.** Right clavicle (mid-shaft, two separate events — first c. age 14, the second a refracture roughly eighteen months later, the second healing with a palpable callus that remains visible as a slight asymmetry under his t-shirt); left distal radius (greenstick, c. age 13, set by carnival doctor without imaging); right fifth metacarpal (boxer's fracture, c. age 17, etiology disputed — Blaze claimed a fall, Crash suspected a fight); multiple non-displaced rib fractures (at least four documented incidents, likely more, all managed with binding and time); right fibula (spiral, c. age 19, sustained in a ramp under-rotation, treated in a county hospital under what may have been the only formal medical encounter of his minority).

**Concussive history, pre-curse.** Minimum of six diagnosable concussions before age 22, by reconstructive estimate. None received formal post-concussion management. Late-Bronze-Age scenes show him rubbing his temples in characteristic post-traumatic headache patterns; the modern medical reader would suspect chronic traumatic encephalopathy as a plausible co-morbid substrate, were the curse not subsequently confounding the picture entirely.

**Road rash, healed.** Extensive, distributed across the lateral surfaces of both legs, both hips, the right shoulder, both elbows, and the dorsal left forearm. The largest single patch, on the right hip, was a third-degree friction burn requiring debridement — he carries (carried) a thirty-square-inch hypopigmented scar there from his late teens, photographically attested in Aaron-era flashbacks.

**Burns.** Fire-stunt work produced first- and second-degree burns repeatedly across the dorsal hands, forearms, and lower face. By age 20, Blaze had a working baseline relationship with burn pain that no civilian adult would have. *This is psychologically relevant: when the curse arrives and consumes him in fire nightly, he is not encountering a novel sensation. He is encountering an old one at impossible amplitude.*

**Soft tissue.** Chronic low-back strain by age 21; right rotator cuff tendinopathy (the throttle-hand shoulder) by age 22.

---

## III. THE TRANSFORMATION AS MEDICAL EVENT

The Zarathos bonding (*Marvel Spotlight* #5, c. age 21–22) is not classifiable within any human medical taxonomy and must be described phenomenologically.

**The event itself.** Skin, hair, and superficial tissues of the head, neck, hands, and (when full-bodied) trunk and limbs are *consumed* — the canonical depiction is combustion without ash, replaced by visible osseous structure wreathed in flame at sustained temperatures inconsistent with the persistence of underlying tissue. Yet the underlying tissue persists. Reversion restores the body to its pre-transformation configuration with apparent fidelity, minus accumulated incidental injuries.

**Physiological correlates, inferred from depicted behavior.** During transformation: no respiration visible, no pulse palpable in flame-state combatants who have grappled him (multiple sources), apparent indifference to ambient temperature, immunity to most conventional ballistic and edged trauma in the form of *non-persistence* rather than imperviousness (wounds open and close), and a marked alteration of voice, posture, and proprioception. Pre-Aaron, post-reversion fatigue is severe — he sleeps hard, eats voraciously, and shows the metabolic signature of a body that has been doing enormous work it cannot remember. Post-Aaron, this attenuates.

**Cyclical pattern.** Originally nocturnal — dusk-triggered, dawn-reverting — which constituted, for years, a *de facto* circadian disorder of supernatural origin. Blaze's sleep architecture in the 1970s is functionally that of a chronic shift-worker who is also being assaulted nightly: brief diurnal sleep, frequently interrupted, low slow-wave proportion implied by his perpetual exhaustion. Mid-1980s onward, the trigger shifts to *proximity to evil* (Mackie era's "innocent blood" sensitivity), which removes the predictability without restoring the rest. Aaron-era and forward: largely volitional, though stress, alcohol, and acute injury all lower the threshold.

**Memory and continuity.** In the early continuity, Blaze does *not* retain coherent memory of Rider-actions. He wakes in unfamiliar locations, with knowledge of having done things he cannot specify, occasionally beside bodies. This is, in every functionally relevant sense, a *dissociative fugue disorder of supernatural etiology*. By the modern era, integration has improved and he retains the actions; he has not, however, made peace with them. He has only stopped being surprised.

**The Penance Stare as somatic event.** When deployed, the Stare appears to require Blaze (or the Rider sharing his eyes) to *receive*, in compressed form, the totality of suffering inflicted by the target. The recipient's collapse is dramatic; Blaze's own post-Stare affect is consistently flat-to-shaken. The cumulative load — decades of absorbed atrocity, replayed first-person — constitutes its own traumatic exposure, distinct from and additive to everything else. He has never been debriefed for it. There is no protocol.

---

## IV. POST-CURSE INJURY LEDGER

Because most non-supernatural trauma resolves with transformation, the persistent injury ledger is shorter than the *event* ledger, which is enormous. Selected events of medical significance:

- **Multiple impalings**, by demonic and human weapons alike, across all eras. The Mackie-era hellfire shotgun work produced reciprocal injuries — Blaze took buckshot, edged weapons, and a documented spear-through-torso (vol. 3, mid-run) without persistent sequelae beyond a few days of guarded movement.
- **Decapitation**, at least twice (Aaron era and Cates-adjacent), with reconstitution. The psychological aftermath of decapitation-and-return is undescribed in canon because Blaze does not describe it. He resumes the next panel.
- **Soul extraction**, by Mephisto (multiple), Blackheart (*Rise of the Midnight Sons*–era and after), and others. Each extraction constitutes, in effect, a near-death experience with the additional metaphysical violation of personal-essence theft. Blaze's affect after each is notably constricted for weeks of in-story time.
- **De-bonding from Zarathos** (*Ghost Rider* vol. 2 #81, Isabella, and again in Aaron's run). These periods produce something resembling withdrawal: irritability, sleep disturbance, a paradoxical sense of incompleteness in a man who has spent decades wanting nothing more than separation. The body that has known the Rider for decades does not know how to be only itself.
- **Re-bonding and "World Rider" augmentation** (Aaron, *Fear Itself: The Fearless*): multiple Spirits inhabiting one body. The depicted instability of this period — overreach, judgment lapses, somatic discomfort — is consistent with a body asked to host more than its architecture was built for.
- **King of Hell physiological alterations** (Cates, *Damnation* and after): the somatic envelope is altered by office. Reports of altered eye-light, augmented flame, throne-bound dissociative episodes. He occupies the body of an infernal sovereign with the affect of a man wearing a borrowed suit.
- **Possession by undiluted Zarathos.** On the occasions when Zarathos has slipped governance entirely, Blaze's body has been used in ways he experiences post hoc as violation. This is, structurally, *bodily autonomy injury* repeated across decades, and is the somatic substrate of his refusal to inhabit his body as a settled home.

**Cumulative effect.** No persistent disability in the conventional sense; instead, a *characterological* disability — a man who has stopped trusting his skin to remain his, and who has accordingly stopped investing in it as a site of pleasure, comfort, or rest.

---

## V. SUBSTANCE HISTORY

**Alcohol.** The longitudinally consistent substance. Pattern across eras: solitary, nocturnal, anesthetic. Roadside dive bars, motel rooms, the basement of wherever he is currently quartered. Drink of preference varies (whiskey predominant in Mackie and Aaron eras; beer as workmanlike baseline), but the *function* is constant. He does not drink to celebrate, to socialize, or to enhance — he drinks to dim. The pour is heavy, the pace is steady, the cutoff is unconsciousness or interruption. He shows no observable acute withdrawal during enforced sobriety on Avengers deployment, suggesting tolerance without full physiological dependence — *functional alcohol use disorder, moderate*, in DSM-5-TR terms. He drinks before he sleeps because he cannot sleep otherwise. He drinks after a Stare because he has just absorbed a life's worth of cruelty and has no other container. The Rider's metabolism almost certainly clears ethanol abnormally, which means he must drink *more* than a comparable mortal to achieve effect, which he does.

**Tobacco.** Intermittent across eras. Cigarettes during certain Bronze Age and Mackie sequences; cigars in scattered modern appearances. Never described as nicotine-dependent; reads as situational, anchored to particular bars, particular waits, particular companions. Probably down across the modern era.

**Caffeine.** Continuous and high. Diner coffee, refilled. Black. He is the customer waitresses do not have to ask twice.

**Illicit substances.** None of significance in the canonical record. Notable for a man with his trauma load, his social environments (carnival, biker bars, dive culture), and his serial proximity to controlled-substance economies. The abstention is, in its own right, a datum: alcohol is permitted because it is *paternal* in his history (Crash drank), socially indistinguishable from the bar environments he inhabits, and easily moralized as ordinary. Harder substances would require him to think of himself as a user, which his self-concept will not permit. He is damned, not dissolute.

**Prescription medication.** None documented. He has not, across six decades of canonical record, been depicted accepting a prescription, attending a follow-up, or filling a pharmacy order. The healthcare system is one of the institutions he is not in.

---

## VI. SLEEP

Disordered, chronically, by every available metric.

Early continuity: transformation triggered at sleep onset, producing a phobic avoidance of falling asleep that compounded a baseline insomnia. He learned to nap in fragments, in daylight, in motel rooms with the curtains drawn — a pattern that persisted past the trigger's evolution because the *learned avoidance* outlasted the *original danger*. Mackie era: bar-to-bed-to-nightmare cycle, repeated. Aaron and after: nightmares attested but not centralized; chronic short sleep implied by his perpetually low-energy presentation in non-combat scenes.

Sleep position, where depicted: supine, fully clothed including boots in motel scenes, jacket within arm's reach, weapons accessible. He sleeps the way men who have been attacked while sleeping sleep. He has been.

Dream content, where canonically rendered: predominantly Crash Simpson's death, his mother walking away, Roxanne's various losses, and a recurrent figure of fire he does not name. He does not discuss them.

---

## VII. NUTRITION, METABOLISM, EXERTION

**Eating pattern.** Erratic. Diner meals, gas-station food, occasional binge after transformation depletion. No prepared kitchen, no domestic routine — he does not cook because he does not have a kitchen because he does not have a home. Caloric intake skews high after Rider events. He has been seen putting away a full diner breakfast plus a second order without comment from servers who clearly recognize the type.

**Exercise.** No deliberate regimen; instead, the constant low-grade exertion of riding (postural endurance, isometric grip and core), occasional mechanical labor on the bike, and the irregular but extreme exertion of combat. He does not run for fitness, lift weights, or attend any structured physical practice. His body is maintained the way a working mechanic's hands are maintained — by use.

**Pain processing.** Markedly abnormal. Pain is, for Blaze, *information about whether something has reached him*, not a signal demanding cessation of the painful activity. He walks off injuries that would put a civilian in an ambulance. This is not stoicism in the virtuous sense; it is the predictable end-state of a nervous system that has been overwritten so many times by transformation-grade noxious stimulus that ordinary noxious stimulus reads as background. He has, in effect, a chronic *hypoalgesic* presentation that masks the actual injury burden and would, in a non-supernatural patient, be a significant clinical concern.

---

## VIII. SEXUAL AND REPRODUCTIVE HISTORY

Sparse, tragic, and structurally compromised by every other element of his life.

Roxanne Simpson is the central romantic-sexual attachment of his life. Their physical relationship is depicted with restraint befitting the eras of publication but is plainly the central erotic fact of his biography. The Aaron-era continuity provides a son. The son is lost. The lineage is lost. Subsequent depicted romantic interest is minimal and typically aborted by Blaze himself before consummation or commitment.

His libido does not appear divorced from attachment. He is not depicted as a man of casual sexual life, despite decades of road and bar settings that would afford abundant opportunity. The abstention is consistent with the broader anhedonic-ascetic pattern: pleasure is suspect, intimacy is dangerous, and his body is not a safe instrument with which to offer either.

Reproductive: one son, attested, lost. Whatever the curse has done to his genetic continuity is unrecorded.

---

## IX. SURGICAL / PROCEDURAL HISTORY

Effectively none in the conventional record. He has not been operated on by a surgeon to canonical knowledge; injuries that would have required surgery have either healed via reversion or been treated by mystical intervention. He has been "operated on" in metaphysical registers — soul extractions, ritual re-bondings, exorcism attempts, the temporary stripping of the Rider — each of which functions, psychologically, as a non-consensual or marginally-consented invasive procedure with no anesthesia and no recovery protocol. The cumulative effect on his relationship to bodily integrity is severe.

---

## X. PSYCHOLOGICAL IMPACT, INTEGRATED

Each of the foregoing produces a specific psychological residue, and the residues interact.

The pre-curse fracture-and-burn ledger taught him, before he was twenty, that *the body is a tool you operate until it fails, then patch and operate again.* This was a workable schema for a stunt rider. It is a catastrophic schema for a man who would subsequently spend fifty years inhabiting a body subject to nightly annihilation: it pre-licensed his refusal to grieve his own physical losses.

The transformation taught him *the body is not reliably yours.* The early fugues taught him *your actions are not reliably yours.* The soul extractions taught him *even your essence is not reliably yours.* The cumulative lesson — which he has organized his entire interpersonal life around — is that *nothing about the self is a stable foundation for promises to others,* which is why he makes none.

The drinking is the anesthetic against the absorbed Stares and the night-thoughts; the insomnia is the residue of decades of nocturnal trigger; the hypoalgesia is the nervous system's adaptation to a noxious load no human design contemplated. The asceticism — the refusal of pleasure, the saddlebag life, the basement quarters — is partly characterological restitution, partly the practical recognition of a man who has learned not to accumulate what will be taken.

He has the body of a long-distance survivor of a war no one else has fought, and the medical record one would predict from such a survivor, if such a survivor existed. He has never seen a clinician who could read it.

He is not coming in for a follow-up.


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: JOHN "JOHNNY" BLAZE

*Compiled from longitudinal observation; cross-indexed with combat footage, civilian-pattern surveillance, intimate-distance witness reports, and inferred reconstruction from published record (1972–present).*

---

## I. BASELINE MORPHOLOGY AND STANDING POSTURE

Subject presents at approximately 6'1" / 185 cm, weight cycling between 175 and 195 lbs depending on era of observation, with the lean-muscled wire-frame of a man who built his body through stunt riding rather than gym work — overdeveloped forearms, wrists, and grip musculature consistent with decades of throttle-and-clutch handling; shoulders carried slightly forward of plumb (chronic motorcycle posture); thoracic spine showing mild kyphotic set; lumbar musculature hypertrophied asymmetrically (right side dominant from repeated kick-starting and from the habitual mounted lean). Pelvis carried in slight posterior tilt — a man who has spent more of his adult hours seated on a bike than standing. Hip flexors chronically shortened. Hamstrings reciprocally tight. Calf development asymmetric, right gastrocnemius marginally larger (rear brake foot).

Standing at rest, subject distributes weight 60/40 to the left leg, freeing the right for movement — a stance characteristic of someone who expects to need to step, kick, or mount within the next few seconds. The hands almost never hang fully relaxed at the sides. They occupy themselves: thumb hooked in belt loop, palm flattened against the hip pocket where a lighter rides, or one hand wrapped around the opposite wrist in front of the body — never the schoolboy "behind the back" clasp, which would close his weapon line.

Head carriage is slightly forward of the shoulders, chin tucked a few degrees down, gaze raised under the brow. This produces the characteristic *watching from beneath the hairline* affect noted by virtually every civilian who has tried to describe him afterward. The result is that strangers consistently overestimate his hostility and underestimate his attention.

---

## II. GAIT AND LOCOMOTION

**Unloaded walking gait.** Heel strike moderate, mid-stance brief, push-off conservative. Stride length shorter than his leg length would predict — the walk of a man minimizing energy expenditure across long arbitrary distances. Cadence steady, near-metronomic at roughly 110 steps per minute on flat ground. Arms swing minimally; right arm marginally more constrained than left (residual guarding of the throttle hand from old fracture sites). He does not look down at his feet. He does not look up at signage. He scans at horizon-level and lets peripheral vision handle the rest.

**Approach to a bike.** Pace lengthens by perhaps fifteen percent in the final ten yards. Right hand finds the key in the watch-pocket of his jeans (or, in eras where the bike is keyless/hellfire-bonded, traces the same micro-motion as a vestigial gesture). He mounts left-side, swinging the right leg over without breaking visual scan of his surroundings — a habit forged in carnival lots where bikes and crowds and idiots commingled.

**Walking with a woman or child he is protecting.** Subject positions himself on the curbside or threat-side automatically, a placement so consistent that it functions as a tell: identify the side Blaze walks on and you have identified what he believes the threat vector is. Pace shortens to match the protectee's.

**Walking into a room he distrusts** (bar, church, government building, Avengers common areas in the Aaron run): pace slows by perhaps ten percent, shoulders square fractionally, hands come out of pockets, weight redistributes 50/50, gaze sweeps from far corner to near corner before he commits past the threshold. He never stops in a doorway — he is always either out or in.

**Combat locomotion.** Surprisingly economical. No flourish, no telegraphing. Closes ground in straight lines unless terrain demands otherwise. Footwork is brawler-flat rather than martial-artist precise. He fights, and he rides, like a man who learned both by surviving them rather than by being taught.

---

## III. THE HANDS

Disproportionately important to the file. Hands are working hands: knuckles thickened and slightly displaced from old breaks; calluses across the palmar pads at the base of the fingers from grip work; a chronic callus on the inside of the right index finger's middle phalanx (brake lever); nicotine staining on the right index-middle fingers in eras of active tobacco use, fading in eras of cessation. Nails kept short, irregularly trimmed — bitten when stressed, especially the right thumbnail. Cuticles ragged. The hands are scarred in a constellation diagnostic of mechanical work: small burn marks across the back of the left hand (exhaust pipes), a long thin scar across the right palm (something sharp, gripped reflexively), assorted small lacerations on the knuckles.

**At rest:** Hands occupy themselves. He turns objects in them — a Zippo, a bottle cap, a spent shell casing, a coin. The turning is rhythmic, not anxious-fast. He does not fidget at high frequency; he fidgets at low frequency, like a man who has accepted that he will be waiting.

**In conversation:** Minimal gesticulation. When he does gesture, it is from the elbow rather than the shoulder, small movements close to the body. He does not point with the finger; he points with a slight chin lift or, occasionally, with the lit end of a cigarette.

**Under stress:** The dominant hand finds an object to grip and the grip is sustained until the stress resolves. The non-dominant hand drifts to the back of the neck, to the jaw, or — most diagnostically — to the sternum, where it rests flat for a count of two or three before withdrawing. This is read as an unconscious somatic check of the location where the transformation initiates.

**In intimacy** (the rare cases on record — Roxanne, primarily): Hands become unusually still. He is a man who, when he chooses to touch someone he loves, does it slowly and once, rather than repeatedly and lightly. Palm placement is firm, weighted, and prolonged. He does not stroke; he holds.

---

## IV. THE FACE

**Resting facial state.** Mouth slightly downturned at the corners — not a frown, a settled neutral. Jaw musculature visibly developed from chronic bruxism. Crow's-feet pronounced for his age, asymmetric (deeper on the right, which is the side he squints when riding into low sun). Brow heavy, set low, with a vertical glabellar furrow worn deep enough to read as permanent. Two finer parallel furrows across the forehead, visible only when he raises the brow.

**Eyes.** Blue, set deep beneath the orbital ridge. Blink rate measurably depressed compared to civilian baseline — approximately 8–10 blinks per minute at rest, against a civilian norm of 15–20. This is a stunt-rider's adaptation (you cannot blink mid-air) that has become a personality artifact: it gives the eye contact its characteristic unsettling duration. Pupil response normal except in proximity to supernatural triggers, where surveillance has noted brief unilateral pupillary asymmetry preceding transformation.

**Smile.** Rare. When present, asymmetric — the left corner rises higher than the right. Does not reach the eyes in social contexts; reaches the eyes only in narrow circumstances: a child unharmed after a near-miss, a motorcycle starting on the first kick, a memory of Crash Simpson surfacing unbidden. The smile, when genuine, is brief — averaging under two seconds before he closes it.

**Tells.**
- **Pre-transformation:** A single hard swallow; jaw clench; the right hand opening and closing once; brief downward gaze; a slow exhale through the nose.
- **Anger building:** Stillness rather than movement. He goes *quieter* and *more economical* as he escalates. The dangerous Blaze is the still one.
- **Lie detection:** When he disbelieves someone, his head tilts a few degrees to the right and his blink rate drops further. He does not interrupt; he lets them finish, then says nothing for an interval long enough to make them either elaborate or recant.
- **Grief surfacing:** The jaw unsets briefly, lips part by a millimeter, then re-close. He does not weep visibly on the record. The pattern is: a single deep inhale, eyes off-focus to middle distance, then a brisk return to task.
- **Being thanked, complimented, or called good:** Eyes drop. Head turns three to ten degrees off the speaker's axis. Verbal response truncated to a syllable. This is one of the most reliable behavioral signatures in the file.

---

## V. GROOMING AND PRESENTATION

Hair worn medium-long in most eras, sandy-blond darkening toward dirty-blond in adulthood, allowed to grow until it physically interferes with vision, then cut — often by his own hand or by a partner, irregularly. He does not visit barbers. Facial hair maintained at perpetual two-to-four-day stubble; he shaves when a mission or social demand requires it, not on schedule. Shower frequency is adequate but unceremonious — washes off the road, the smoke, the blood, in that order, and does not linger.

Wardrobe is a uniform with minor variants: dark denim, plain T-shirt or long-sleeve henley, leather jacket (usually with carnival-era accents or studded reinforcement at the shoulders), boots. He owns clothing measured in days, not seasons. He does not have a wallet so much as a folded sheaf of cash and one or two documents wrapped in a rubber band. He does not wear jewelry except, in certain eras, a small medallion or token related to Roxanne or his lost son, kept under the shirt rather than displayed.

He smells of: gasoline, leather conditioner, cheap soap, road dust, intermittently cigarette smoke, and (post-transformation, for hours afterward) a faint ozone-sulfur trace that civilians register without identifying. He does not wear cologne. He does not own deodorant of any expressive brand.

---

## VI. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

Subject sleeps in fragments. Total sleep time averages four to five hours in a twenty-four-hour cycle, distributed across two or three episodes rather than consolidated. Preferred sleep position: supine, arms at sides or one across the chest, in a configuration that surveillance has noted resembles a corpse-pose more than a relaxed sleeper. He does not sleep on his side facing a wall; he sleeps facing the door of whatever room he is in, even when this requires repositioning the bed.

Sleep onset latency: long. He lies awake for thirty to ninety minutes before sleep, usually with one hand behind the head and the other on his sternum (the transformation-check posture). REM episodes are disrupted; subject is observed to wake abruptly, sit upright, and remain motionless for ten to thirty seconds before lying back down. Verbalization in sleep is rare but documented — fragmentary, name-fragments ("Roxanne," "Crash," "Dad"), and the occasional unintelligible syllable.

He cannot sleep in soft beds without difficulty. Hotel rooms: he is more likely to sleep on top of the made cover than under it, fully clothed minus boots, jacket within reach. Avengers compound quarters (Aaron's run): he sleeps in the basement, on a cot, with the bike parked inside the room.

He does not nap. Daytime sleep is foreclosed by old transformation-trigger conditioning (nightfall as trigger in early continuity left him with an internalized hypervigilance about being supine during waking hours). He will lie down with eyes open; he will not sleep.

---

## VII. EATING

Eats infrequently, quickly, and without ceremony. Diet is roadside American: diner breakfasts (eggs, bacon, black coffee, toast), burgers, chili, sandwiches eaten standing at gas-station counters. He prefers food he can eat with one hand. He drinks coffee constantly — black, no sugar, accepted at any temperature including cold. He does not order dessert. He does not finish meals; he eats until functional and pushes the plate aside.

He chews on the left side of his mouth preferentially — old molar work on the right, presumably uncorrected. He cuts food with the side of the fork when possible to avoid two-handed eating. In a booth, he sits with his back to the wall and his eyes to the door, always.

He does not cook. On the rare occasions when he prepares food, it is canned, heated in the can, eaten from the can. The exception is coffee: he is particular about coffee, and will brew it from grounds rather than instant when he has the means.

---

## VIII. DRINKING — PATTERN AND POSTURE

Bar setting, almost archetypal: subject enters, scans, takes a stool at the corner of the bar (back to the wall, side-angled view of the door), orders whiskey or beer (whiskey in the harder eras, beer when he is trying to slow himself), pays in advance with cash. He does not run a tab. He drinks methodically rather than greedily — the first drink is held for a long interval; subsequent drinks accelerate. He does not engage strangers. He nods at the bartender. He does not eat the bar nuts.

Posture at the bar: forearms on the wood, weight forward, head down between the shoulders, gaze on the glass rather than the room. This is the only context in which he stops scanning, and it is a deliberate withdrawal of vigilance — the drinking is, partially, a permission to stop watching.

Threshold for visible impairment is high; he has functional tolerance. The signs that he is over his line: speech slows further (he is already slow; he becomes slower); the right hand finds his face and stays there longer than usual; the left side of the mouth turns up infrequently in a private half-smile at nothing. He does not become belligerent drunk. He becomes geological drunk — slower, heavier, more silent.

---

## IX. SMOKING AND ORAL HABITS

In eras of active tobacco use: cigarettes held between right index and middle finger, lit one-handed with a Zippo whose flip-and-strike is a discrete two-beat motion he can execute without looking. He does not smoke chain-fashion; he smokes one, finishes it, and then does not light another for an interval. He pinches the cherry between thumb and forefinger to extinguish when no ashtray is available — a habit producing characteristic small burn scars on the right thumbpad.

Oral habits: jaw clenching (chronic, bilateral, with measurable masseter hypertrophy); occasional tongue against the inside of the cheek when thinking; minimal lip-licking. He does not whistle. He hums rarely, in private, fragments of carnival-era music — calliope tunes, country radio of the seventies, songs his father played.

---

## X. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE PATTERNS

Sparse data; the file relies on inference from the narrow record. Subject is not promiscuous. Sexual activity is bound to attachment — Roxanne is the only sustained sexual partner across decades of observation, with intermittent gaps and brief secondary relationships in non-Roxanne eras (notably implied during the Mackie period and the Aaron mid-run, never lingered on).

In intimacy he is reported as: physically careful, slow to initiate, prone to withdrawing afterward to the edge of the bed or to a chair across the room within an hour. He does not sleep beside a partner through a full night — the same insomnia and trigger-vigilance that govern his solo sleep govern his shared sleep, and partners across eras have remarked on waking to find him gone from the bed, sitting at a window or on a stair, smoking.

Touch threshold is low for warmth (he leans into a hand on his shoulder, briefly) and high for surprise (a touch from behind produces a fast pivot, fist half-raised, contained within a half-second — a reflex he cannot fully suppress and that he has clearly trained himself to abort). He does not initiate physical affection in public.

---

## XI. RIDING POSTURE — THE PRIMARY HABITAT

He is more himself on the bike than off it. The riding posture is the home posture: torso angled forward perhaps fifteen to twenty degrees off vertical, weight on the wrists distributed against the bars without locking the elbows, knees gripping the tank with the inside-thigh musculature he has built since childhood, feet finding the pegs without visual reference. Helmet use is era-variable and often refused (the transformation renders helmets cosmetic).

He countersteers cleanly, leans into corners further than civilian riders find comfortable, and brakes late. He does not weave through traffic so much as part it. Idling at a stoplight, he keeps the bike in gear, left hand on the clutch, right foot down — a stance that permits immediate departure. He does not put the kickstand down at a stoplight, ever.

On the road for long hauls, his face goes empty in a way it does not go in any other context. The motor noise functions as auditory white-out, the wind as somatic anesthetic, the vibration as a kind of cradle. This is the closest he comes to rest. Surveillance has noted that he will ride for sixteen-hour stretches without stopping for anything but fuel and will appear, on dismounting, to be in a mild dissociative state — slow to speak, slow to focus — for several minutes afterward.

---

## XII. STATE-DEPENDENT SHIFTS — A REFERENCE TABLE

**Calm (rare, brief, usually solitary, usually mounted).** Shoulders drop a quarter-inch. Jaw unsets. Right hand opens and closes once and then rests. Blink rate normalizes briefly. Half-smile appears at nothing. Hums.

**Mild stress (social demand, unfamiliar setting).** Hands out of pockets. Weight redistributes. Scan increases. Verbal output shortens. Drinks if available.

**Moderate stress (perceived deceit, authority figure pressing him, being thanked).** Goes still. Head tilts slightly. Blink rate drops. Pauses long enough to be uncomfortable. Withdraws physically — steps back, turns a shoulder away, finds an exit angle.

**Threat to self.** Curiously relaxed. Stance opens. Hands come up to a low ready. Expression goes flat. He has metabolized personal danger into something close to indifference, and it shows.

**Threat to a third party (child especially).** The transformation tell-sequence initiates: swallow, jaw clench, hand to sternum, exhale. Voice drops half an octave. Movement becomes economical to the point of looking slow until the moment of action, at which point he is faster than the witness can register.

**Post-transformation, civilian-form return.** Several seconds of disorientation — eyes unfocused, body slack against whatever surface is nearest, audible breath. He often kneels or sits within the first half-minute. Hands tremble briefly. He does not speak for one to three minutes. He smells of ozone and burned hair. He will refuse offered water, food, or contact, and walk it off alone if permitted.

**Intimacy (the rare condition).** Hands still. Eyes lower. Speech softens to a register no one outside that distance hears. Holds longer than he touches. Leaves earlier than expected.

**Sleep, true.** Supine. Hand on sternum. Face slack. Mouth slightly open. The only condition in which the glabellar furrow partially relaxes.

---

## XIII. RESIDUAL SIGNATURES

Wherever subject has been for more than an hour, the room retains: a faint smell of leather and gasoline; one or two cigarette ends (in active-smoking eras) crushed flat rather than ground out; an arrangement of small objects (coins, caps, casings) in a short line on a flat surface, which he has turned in his hands and set down without thinking. Chairs he has occupied are pulled back from tables further than necessary. Doors he has passed through are left ajar by a hand's width — never fully closed, never fully open. These are the artifacts a careful surveillant learns to read before the man himself appears in any frame.


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS — SUBJECT: JOHN BLAZE

---

## I. Attachment Classification

The operative classification is **disorganized attachment with avoidant-dismissive overlay and an intermittent anxious-preoccupied substrate that surfaces only around a single bonded figure at a time**. In adult attachment terms, he is a fearful-avoidant who has spent fifty years calcifying the avoidant pole into a way of life while never quite extinguishing the underlying yearning. The disorganization — that is, the simultaneous impulse to approach and to flee a caregiver-equivalent — is the engine; the avoidance is the management strategy he has refined into something resembling personality.

The diagnostic giveaway is not the withdrawal itself. Many traumatized men withdraw. The giveaway is the *quality* of his withdrawals: they occur most reliably **after** a moment of genuine closeness, not before. He does not flee threat; he flees safety. Roxanne, Doctor Strange, Daniel Ketch, the Avengers — the rupture is invariably preceded by a scene of warmth that Blaze finds intolerable to hold. The intolerable element is not the other person; it is the future that closeness implies, the futurity itself, the obligation to be available in the tomorrow he does not believe he will survive intact.

---

## II. Origins of the Pattern

Four developmental insults compound:

1. **Father's death (Barton Blaze) in front of an audience.** The foundational schema: the parental body is a performance object that can be destroyed at any moment, and the crowd will keep watching. Love is something staged for strangers and then ends. Note that Johnny goes on to monetize the exact behavior that killed his father — this is not coincidence but identification with the aggressor (in this case, the aggressor is the stunt itself, the gravity, the bike). To master the thing that took the father is to belatedly protect him.

2. **Maternal disappearance (Naomi Kale).** Worse than death because unaccompanied by ceremony, narrative, or closure. A child cannot grieve what has not been named as lost. The mother becomes the prototype for *every figure who will leave without explanation,* and Blaze, decades later, has internalized that template so thoroughly that he pre-emptively occupies the leaver's position in every dyad. Better to be Naomi than Johnny-watching-Naomi-go.

3. **Crash and Mona Simpson's conditional foster love.** The carnival family loved him, but the carnival was a business and his place in it was earned. Affection bundled with utility produces an adult who cannot accept affection unbundled from utility — when the Avengers offer him a chair at the table on no grounds but membership, he relocates to the basement. He does not know how to be loved for nothing.

4. **The Mephisto bargain.** The structural lesson is the operational catastrophe: when he extends himself maximally in love (offering his soul to save Crash), he is defrauded and Crash dies anyway. Henceforth, **maximum love produces maximum loss plus humiliation.** Every subsequent intimate offering is therefore underwritten by an expectation of double penalty.

---

## III. How He Bonds

Blaze bonds slowly, asymmetrically, and almost always under duress. He does not form relationships in conditions of leisure; he forms them in crisis, and crisis is a context he can manage because it makes the terms of contact concrete and time-limited. A woman pinned in a wrecked car, a child in a basement, a fellow rider down on a shoulder — these are the openings in which Blaze becomes legible to another person. He is exceptional at the first forty-eight hours of an attachment and unreliable after the ninetieth day.

The bonding signs, in order of appearance:

- **Reduction in verbal economy.** Baseline Blaze speaks in clauses; bonded Blaze speaks in sentences. The word count itself is a useful telemetric.
- **Use of given names.** He defaults to "ma'am," "pal," "chief," "kid." When he uses a first name unprompted, a transition has occurred.
- **Mechanical care.** He services the other person's vehicle, checks their tires, tightens something on their porch. Concrete, hand-mediated, transactional-looking care is his idiom for affection; he cannot say "I value you," but he can replace your brake pads.
- **Sharing of food in silence.** A coffee pushed across a counter without comment. He is comfortable in shared silence with very few people; the company he can be silent with is the company he loves.
- **Proximity to sleep.** He is profoundly insomniac and guards his sleep zone; allowing another body within twenty feet of him during a sleep attempt is a near-maximal trust signal. With Roxanne, eventually, he sleeps. With almost no one else.

He does **not** bond through disclosure, eye contact, physical demonstration, or shared positive activity. He has no skill at any of these. He bonds through co-survival and small repaired objects.

---

## IV. How He Distrusts

Distrust is his default and requires no provocation; the question is not what triggers his suspicion but what suspends it. The suspension is always provisional. Even with bonded figures, he runs continuous low-grade integrity audits: Did she ask about my last week? Did he look away when I mentioned the Stare? Did the offer come with conditions I missed?

The distrust pattern is **stratified by source type:**

- **Institutional / theological.** Maximal. Heaven, Hell, the Catholic Church, the Avengers as institution (distinct from individual Avengers), S.H.I.E.L.D., any government, any kingdom — distrusted absolutely and pre-emptively. Zadkiel weaponized this distrust into a permanent grievance; no entity claiming divine sanction will ever again receive even procedural credit from him.
- **Powerful individuals.** High distrust. Doctor Strange, Stark, Doom — he reads them as men who will use him and tells himself this is acceptable provided the use produces results he can endorse. He does not expect reciprocity; he expects competent exploitation.
- **Peers in suffering.** Lower distrust. Other Riders, other damned men, men with curses of their own — he extends a baseline credit he extends to no one else. The credit is calibrated against the visible cost the other person is paying; he trusts people who are losing something.
- **Women he could love.** Highest distrust **of his own conduct toward them,** not of them. He believes himself the threat. He runs the audit on whether the relationship will damage her, never whether she will damage him.
- **Children.** Zero distrust. The only category. He extends children unconditional faith and unconditional defense and reads any adult who manipulates a child as instantly disqualified from the species.

---

## V. How He Betrays

Blaze does not betray actively. He betrays through **withdrawal, omission, and pre-emption** — the avoidant's three idioms. The pattern, repeated:

1. **He fails to inform.** He does not tell Roxanne when he is leaving, when he is in danger, when he has accepted a job that will take him under. The omission is rationalized as protection ("she's safer not knowing") but functions as control: the unilateral decision preserves his exit.
2. **He pre-empts the other's choice.** Rather than allow Roxanne, Ketch, or Strange to decide whether to continue with him under new conditions, he decides for them and removes himself. He calls this mercy. It is the structural opposite of mercy; it is the denial of the other's agency to consent to a difficulty.
3. **He breaks promises by going silent rather than refusing.** He will say yes and then disappear, which is worse than no. He knows it is worse. He cannot make himself say no, because saying no would require him to occupy a position in another person's life long enough to decline it.
4. **He underdelivers on stated intimacy commitments.** When he does promise return, presence, fatherhood, husbandhood — the promise is made earnestly and abandoned non-maliciously, which does not relieve the damage.

He is rarely the betrayer in the moral sense. He is almost always the disappointment in the structural sense. The two feel identical to the betrayed.

---

## VI. How He Repairs

Repair is his weakest interpersonal capacity, and the deficit is instructive. He has three repair moves, in escalating order of cost, and all three are non-verbal:

1. **Return.** He simply appears again — at the door, at the diner, at the grave — months or years later, on the assumption that presence after absence constitutes apology. It does not, but he does not know how to say more.
2. **Tangible labor.** He fixes the thing in her house that is broken. He buries the body. He pays the debt the betrayed person did not know he owed. The labor is the apology rendered in his only fluent dialect.
3. **Standing the watch.** The maximal repair: he positions himself as silent permanent guardian of the wronged party's perimeter, often without their knowledge, sometimes for years. He has done this for Roxanne in multiple eras. It is not what she wanted; what she wanted was a husband. He gives her a sentinel and considers the books balanced.

He does **not** apologize verbally with any competence. The closest he comes is the phrase "I should have—" left unfinished, the rest absorbed by a long exhale. The unfinished sentence is, in his grammar, the apology.

---

## VII. Intimacy

Sexual intimacy is sparse, almost exclusively love-bonded, and largely undepicted but contextually narrow. He is not sexually adventurous, not promiscuous, not casually receptive. The libido is fused to attachment; outside of bonded contexts, he is functionally asexual by election. This is not religious continence — it is the more elemental refusal to allow the body to commit what the rest of him cannot sustain.

Emotional intimacy, when it occurs, is characterized by:

- **Long silences treated as content, not absence.** With Roxanne especially, the canon shows them sitting wordless on a porch or beside a bike for extended sequences. He is not withholding speech; he is communicating through co-presence, which is, in his lexicon, the deepest available register.
- **Physical proximity without overt contact.** He sits near rather than touches. The shoulder-to-shoulder posture, the hand on the small of a back during passage through a door, the brief grip on a forearm at parting — these constitute his full somatic vocabulary of affection.
- **Confession by metaphor.** He does not say "I am suffering." He says "the bike's been pulling left" or "I haven't been sleeping." A trained partner learns to read the surface complaint as the deeper one.
- **Asymmetric disclosure.** He listens far more than he discloses. He can absorb another person's entire history without offering more than the broad strokes of his own. This is not strategic — it is that her history feels safer to hold than his does.

---

## VIII. Dependency

He is **counter-dependent to a clinically significant degree.** He will accept no help he can plausibly refuse, even at marked cost to himself or the mission. The refusal pattern:

- He does not borrow money.
- He does not accept lodging beyond a single night.
- He does not accept medical care he can self-administer.
- He does not request information he can extract by riding to the location.
- He does not delegate tasks he can perform alone.
- He does not name his needs even when directly asked. The honest answer to "what do you need" is, in his idiom, "nothing" — and "nothing" is sometimes literally true, because the apparatus of needing has been disused for so long it has atrophied.

He **does** accept help in two narrow conditions: (a) when refusal would endanger a third party (he will let Strange portal him if a child's life is on the clock), and (b) when the helper is themselves at the lowest social rung — a waitress's coffee on the house, a fellow drifter's offer of a couch. Help from the powerful triggers refusal; help from the equally-or-more burdened is accepted as fraternal currency.

The counter-dependence is not pride. It is a contract he believes he signed in adolescence: I take nothing because I deserve nothing, and the only way to keep the books from spiraling is to refuse all credit.

---

## IX. The Relational Template, Specified

Across every relationship of significance — Roxanne, Crash, Mona, Ketch, Strange, his son, the Avengers, even Mephisto and Zarathos themselves as perverse attachment objects — the same six-stage template recurs:

1. **Crisis introduction.** They meet under duress. Blaze provides decisive aid.
2. **Asymmetric obligation.** The other party experiences gratitude; Blaze experiences responsibility. The valences are mismatched from the outset.
3. **Tentative deepening.** A period — days, weeks, occasionally months — of provisional closeness, during which Blaze becomes uncharacteristically present. This is the window in which the other party falls in love with him, befriends him, comes to depend on him. The window is real. He is, briefly, available.
4. **The intolerable plateau.** Closeness stabilizes. There is no longer an active crisis. The relationship demands ordinary continuance. Blaze begins to disorganize internally: drinking increases, sleep degrades, he takes longer rides for thinner reasons.
5. **Rupture, usually externally rationalized.** A mission, the curse, an enemy targeting the other party — some external event provides cover for an exit he was already preparing. He frames the departure as protection. He may believe the framing.
6. **The long sentinel posture.** From distance, he watches over the relationship's residue. He defends them from threats they do not know exist. He returns at intervals — funerals, anniversaries, anniversaries of bargains — and is briefly visible before resuming the watch.

Roxanne is the paradigmatic case but not the only one. Ketch follows the template (crisis cooperation → fraternal warmth → withdrawal → distant monitoring). Strange follows it (case-based collaboration → respectful regard → Blaze's eventual ghosting → Strange's annoyed acceptance that this is the relationship's shape). Even his Avengers tenure follows it in compressed form: he showed up when called, performed competently, refused integration, and quartered himself away from the team.

The template's function is **predictive control of loss.** If every relationship ends, then ending them oneself, on one's own schedule, with a rationalization in hand, is the only available form of agency over the loss. He is not avoiding pain — he is rationing it, administering it to himself in scheduled doses rather than receiving it from outside on a timeline he cannot choose. This is the avoidant's bargain, and Blaze has signed it so many times the signature is autonomic.

---

## X. The Two Anomalies

Two relationships break the template, and the breaks are diagnostically rich.

**Zarathos / the Rider.** This is the only attachment Blaze cannot exit. He has tried — exorcism, separation, refusal — and every escape has been temporary. The forced co-presence has produced, against his will, something resembling a working relationship: he negotiates with the Spirit, he loans it his body, he tolerates its company. This is the only relationship in which his counter-dependence has been definitively defeated, and the defeat has had a paradoxically stabilizing effect. He has had to learn to live with someone he cannot leave, and the learning has happened, slowly, against decades of resistance. It is the closest thing to an intimate marriage in his life, and it is with a demon.

**Children, generically.** With children he does not exit. The template does not run. He is briefly present, executes the rescue, and departs — but the departure is not avoidant; it is appropriate, because the child has parents or a system to return to. With children Blaze achieves what he achieves nowhere else: **proportionate intimacy.** He gives what is needed, receives what is offered, and leaves cleanly because the relationship has a natural terminus. One suspects this is the only domain in his life where he is not, structurally, lying — to himself or to the other party — about what is on offer.

These two anomalies are the negative space that reveals the rest of the pattern. The relationships that work for him are the one he cannot escape and the ones that do not require him to stay. Everything in between — the human, optional, sustained, mutual relationships — is the territory he cannot inhabit, and the inability is the wound. Fifty years on the road have not closed it. The road, in fact, is the wound's preferred shape.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS — SUBJECT: JOHN BLAZE

*A longitudinal mapping of the full defensive architecture, organized from primitive to mature, with operational signatures, behavioral tells, observed failure modes, and the prosocial sublimations that constitute the subject's compensatory upper structure. Where defenses fail or invert, the file notes it. Where a defense doubles as a moral achievement, the file notes that too. The thesis the evidence forces: Blaze's defensive system is unusually well-organized for a subject with this trauma load, and the organization is itself diagnostic — he has had fifty years to build it, and the building has cost him every life-good he might otherwise have accumulated.*

---

## I. THE PRIMITIVE TIER

### 1. Splitting — The Foundational Defense

The structural fact of Blaze's psyche is that he carries a second occupant. Canonically the Spirit of Vengeance is an externally-imposed entity; **psychodynamically it functions, and has always functioned, as the receptacle for every disowned self-state Blaze cannot afford to author in the first person.** The convenience of this arrangement is its own indictment. He did not invent Zarathos, but he has, across six decades, learned to *use* him with a fluency that exceeds what any reluctant host would develop.

The behavioral signature is consistent across every writer who has handled him: Blaze refers to the Rider in the third person — "he," "it," "the thing," "the other one," "what's in me." The pronoun choice is never random. It hardens (to "it") when he is most ashamed of an action just performed; it softens (to "he") in moments of grudging alliance; it disappears entirely (collapses into "I") only in the rarest moments of integration, usually in extremis when the cost of maintaining the partition exceeds the cost of dropping it. A surveillance team monitoring his speech could chart his integration state in real time off pronoun selection alone.

The split is targeted, not diffuse. Blaze does not split his perception of others into all-good and all-bad; he reserves the operation for himself. The "good Blaze" is the patient, taciturn, road-weary man who pays for diner coffee and asks about strangers' children. The "bad Blaze," extruded into Zarathos, holds the rage at his mother's abandonment, the resentment at being conscripted by Heaven, the sadistic register required to administer the Penance Stare, the suspicion that he *wanted* the bargain at seventeen and is therefore an accomplice to his own damnation. This last item is the load-bearing freight. He cannot afford to author it. The Rider must.

### 2. Projective Identification of the Disowned Aggression

The split is not static; it is operational. Blaze does not merely *contain* his aggression in the Rider — he *deploys* it through the Rider while preserving the witness-stance of the disapproving spectator. He watches himself burn a man's soul to the membrane of itself and feels, simultaneously, the righteous satisfaction (his) and the horror at the satisfaction (also his, disowned, attributed to the Rider's appetite). The doubled experience is the defense's whole point: it permits the act *and* the moral self-image, in the same body, in the same minute.

This is why his expressions of distaste for the Rider read as sincere and yet never produce any sustained effort at separation once such effort is available. He has had exorcism offered (multiple Bronze Age issues), achieved separation (vol. 2 #81), been de-powered (Aaron), and in every case has returned to the bond within a finite period, citing external necessity. The external necessity is real. The internal necessity — that without the Rider he must own the rage in the first person — is the unspoken second reason.

### 3. Somatization and Bodily Self-Punishment

Blaze does not have a reliable body. Across decades the body has been burned away nightly, impaled, decapitated, stripped of soul, possessed in undiluted form, and physiologically rewritten by an infernal monarchy. The defense he has constructed around this is not denial of pain — he feels it — but **a systematic devaluation of the body as a meaningful site of self.** The body is rental property. Damage to it is not damage to him. Pain is information about the environment, not about the self.

The operational behavior: he does not flinch from foreseeable injury, does not seek medical attention for non-incapacitating wounds, does not maintain the kind of preventive somatic care (sleep, hydration, nutrition, dental, ophthalmologic) that a person who expected to keep the body would maintain. He eats at counters, sleeps in clothes, washes irregularly when traveling. He has been observed to ride for stretches that would produce stress fractures in a stable subject and to walk away from collisions that would hospitalize one. The indifference reads as courage. It is, more accurately, **a chronic low-grade dissociation from somatic ownership** — a defense whose convenience is that it makes him useful in fights and whose cost is that it constitutes a slow-motion passive suicidality he has had fifty years to refine.

### 4. Denial of Authorship Regarding the Original Bargain

The seventeen-year-old who bargained his soul to save Crash Simpson made a decision Blaze has never permitted himself to fully metabolize. The cover story — *I was a child, I was deceived, I was desperate* — is true on its face and yet functions as a denial of the harder facts that are equally true: he made the bargain unilaterally, did not consult Crash, did not consult Roxanne, did not consider the cost-bearer (himself, in eternity), and proceeded from a coping schema (perform impossible risk to keep the family intact) he had absorbed but never examined. The denial preserves him from the more shattering recognition: that the first major decision of his adult life was structurally identical to every decision since, and that the curse is in some sense the *expression* of his character, not its violator.

The behavioral tell: he speaks of the bargain rarely, always in passive voice ("the deal was made," "I was taken in"), and changes the subject within two or three exchanges when interlocutors press. He has never, in any depicted conversation across six decades, narrated the bargain in the first-person active construction it deserves: *I did this.*

---

## II. THE INTERMEDIATE TIER

### 5. Counterdependence

Blaze does not ask. The list of entities he has declined to ask for help, despite available access, is long: Doctor Strange (repeatedly, across decades, despite an explicit standing offer); the Sorcerer Supreme apparatus generally; the Avengers (during the period he was nominally a member, he occupied a basement room and did not request integration into team workflows); his own brother Daniel Ketch, with whom the help-asking would also constitute relationship-building he is unwilling to undertake; Caretaker and the Blood lineage when offered guidance during the Aaron run; and on the negative side, every infernal entity that has proposed alliance.

The defense is rooted in the bargain's lesson: asking is what got Crash killed. Asking is what cost him his soul. Asking, in Blaze's encoded experience, is the act that activates fraudulent counterparties. The safer posture is to absorb the cost privately, render the service required, and depart before reciprocity can be demanded. He pays his own way at counters. He sleeps in his own quarters. He travels alone.

The defense is operationally expensive. He has solved problems alone that a phone call would have shortened; he has taken injuries that allies could have absorbed; he has lost intelligence (about Zadkiel, about the bloodline, about the architecture of his own curse) that available informants would have provided had he tolerated the conversation.

### 6. Geographic Flight as Affect Regulation

When affect rises, Blaze moves. The bike is not merely transportation; it is **the most reliable affect-regulation tool he possesses**, and its reliability is structural — the cognitive load of operating a motorcycle at speed produces an enforced narrowing of attention that displaces intrusive content.
