He has used this mechanism from the Bronze Age (the Friedrich/Mantlo cross-country drift) through the Mackie era (rootless interstate wandering) through the Aaron run (he opens *Ghost Rider* #20 having ridden himself to a dive bar in a town he cannot name) through the modern era, where even his King-of-Hell tenure is interrupted by surface excursions on the bike that no monarch would undertake.

Surveillance implications: he is most stable when in motion and least stable when stationary for periods exceeding roughly seventy-two hours. Containment in a fixed location — team headquarters, infernal throne, hospital, jail, marital home — produces escalating restlessness manifesting first as withdrawal, then as drinking, then as physical departure rationalized post-hoc. He cannot be held in a stationary role; if institutionalized he will erode the role until movement is restored.

### 7. Anesthetic Substance Use

Documented across eras, most prominently in the Mackie run and Aaron's *Ghost Rider* vol. 6: solitary, nocturnal, anesthetic alcohol use, in dive settings, without social context, without the rituals of pleasure (no curated drinks, no toasts, no companion drinkers). The drinking is functional in two senses — it produces sufficient sedation to permit sleep onset, and it provides a narrow window of dulled affect during which the intrusive content (mother's disappearance, Crash's death, Roxanne's serial losses, the bargain, the burning) is metabolically distanced.

Tobacco use intermittent. No depicted illicit drug use of significance. The substance profile is consistent with a functional alcohol use disorder of moderate severity, conducted with the working-class discipline of a man who does not permit it to interfere with operational reliability and would be insulted by the suggestion that he had a problem.

### 8. Reaction Formation Against Grandiosity

Blaze has been offered, in canonical sequence: the power of Heaven (Aaron, by way of Zadkiel's deception), the throne of Hell (Cates), the leadership of the Spirits of Vengeance lineage (multiple writers), divine appointment from the womb (Aaron's retcon), and on smaller scales the leadership of various teams and missions. He has refused, sabotaged, abdicated, or held under protest every one.

The refusal is not virtue alone, although it contains virtue. **It is also a defense against the suspicion that he wanted the original power and is therefore complicit in his damnation.** If he can be observed, by himself, refusing every subsequent offer, the refusals can be tallied against the original acceptance to produce a moral ledger he can almost balance. The asceticism is restitution.

The behavioral signature: when offered authority, he becomes more taciturn than usual, his posture worsens, he refuses food and ceremonial accommodations, he occupies whatever room or quarters he is given as if camping in it rather than inhabiting it, and he undertakes the duties of the role with the minimum effort consistent with not failing them. The King-of-Hell tenure is the paradigm case. He sat on the throne the way a man waits in a county courthouse.

### 9. Anhedonic Asceticism

Distinct from the grandiosity-refusal: a generalized refusal of pleasure. He drinks alone rather than socially; eats for fuel rather than for taste; does not curate music, films, books, food, or scenery despite a life spent on the road that would permit any of these to develop into a private connoisseurship; does not maintain hobbies disconnected from the work; does not collect; does not own beyond the saddlebag standard. The deprivation is restitution. **Every pleasure not taken is an installment against the debt he believes he owes.**

The cost: he has lost the texture of being alive. He does not know, for example, what music he likes outside of what was on the carnival radio in 1969. He does not know what he would order in a restaurant if cost and theater were equal. He has not developed adult taste. He is, in this dimension, arrested at the moment of the bargain — a seventeen-year-old's preferences in a man six decades older, because to develop further would be to claim a self that has not earned the right to preferences.

### 10. Sarcasm Aimed at Authority

A reliable mid-stress tell. When pressed by figures claiming institutional authority — angels, archmagi, Avengers brass, infernal nobility, federal agents in the rare crossover — Blaze deploys a flat, mid-register sarcasm that is not quite insubordination and not quite cooperation. The function is **to register his refusal to accept the authority's framing while not escalating to a fight he would rather avoid.** It also serves as a small, repeated declaration of his theological grievance: every authority is presumed lying until proven otherwise, and the sarcasm acknowledges the presumption without requiring him to litigate it.

The voice is dry, low, undecorated. He does not perform the sarcasm; he delivers it as if reading off a wall. The tell of seriousness, when he means a thing without the protective irony, is the abandonment of sarcasm into declarative plainness — a register shift that interlocutors who know him learn to read as the warning it is.

---

## III. THE HIGHER-ORDER TIER

### 11. Sublimation — The Protection of the Helpless

This is the defense that has done the most work and produced the most good. Blaze has metabolized his own unprotected childhood into **a chronic, durable, prosocial vigilance for the unprotected condition in others** — particularly children, the road-vulnerable (hitchhikers, truckers, runaways, the unhoused proximate to highways), and women in situations of asymmetric danger. The vigilance survives every writer. It survives the King-of-Hell tenure (he runs surface excursions to intervene in incidents that should be beneath his monarch's notice). It survives his depressive episodes. It survives, demonstrably, his own incapacitation — Bronze Age issues show him dragging a broken body toward an incident he cannot ignore.

The defense is, simultaneously, an authentic moral achievement. The file resists the cynicism that would reduce it to mere compensation. He has saved more strangers than any accounting could enumerate, and the saving has been done without the audience he was raised to perform for, without payment, often without acknowledgment, and at consistent cost to himself. **It is the cleanest part of him, and it is clean because it is the only place where the wound and the work coincide without contradiction.**

### 12. Repetition Compulsion, Worked Toward Mastery

He returns, again and again, to the conditions of the original catastrophe: roadside America, stunt-adjacent danger, the rescue of a paternal-figure-equivalent or a child-figure-equivalent from a force he cannot defeat without self-cost. He is, in psychodynamic terms, **re-staging Crash Simpson's death with himself in both roles, trying to author a different ending.** Each iteration is an attempt to render the original loss meaningful by making a subsequent loss preventable.

The compulsion is the negative face of the sublimation. The sublimation makes the protection of strangers a moral achievement; the compulsion makes it an addiction. He cannot stop. Offered retirement, he declines. Offered respite, he refuses. The vigilance is not modulable downward, because modulating it would expose him to the underlying unmetabolized grief.

### 13. Intellectualization, Partial and Theologically Inflected

Blaze is not an intellectual, and the file should not overstate the defense, but he does deploy a constrained intellectualization in his theological framing. He has converted a personal catastrophe into a **cosmological grievance**, which provides the relief of a larger frame: he is not merely a man who lost his soul at seventeen, he is a soldier in a cosmic war that has been rigged against him from before his birth. This frame elevates the suffering, dignifies the resistance, and provides a non-personal explanation for losses that would otherwise be unbearable in their particularity.

The defense is fragile. It works when he is in motion against a clearly-identified cosmic antagonist (Mephisto, Zadkiel, Blackheart). It collapses when the antagonist is intimate (Ketch as brother, his own son's death, Roxanne lost again to ordinary mortality), because intimate losses cannot be elevated into the cosmological register without grotesque inflation.

### 14. Humor, Vestigial

A small defense, easily missed, but present across enough writers to be considered stable: Blaze possesses a dry, bone-deep, working-class humor that surfaces in narrow circumstances — usually with mechanics, diner staff, fellow road-workers, and occasional moments with Ketch or Strange. The humor is **the last visible trace of the boy he was before the bargain.** It does not surface around authority figures, around the curse, or around children in danger. It is the marker, when present, that he is in a moment of unusual psychological safety.

A surveillance team should treat its appearance as diagnostically significant: he is regulated, he is unguarded to a small degree, and he is — briefly — accessible.

### 15. Moral Discipline Around the Use of Force

The most underrated defense. Blaze has the capacity to inflict, through the Penance Stare and through Hellfire generally, harm that approaches the metaphysical maximum: comprehensive empathic correction, soul-burning, irrevocable infernal sentence. He has held this capacity for fifty years. He has, in that time, **maintained an asymmetric targeting discipline** — the Stare and the Hellfire are deployed against predators, never against the powerless, never against bystanders, almost never against the morally ambiguous. The discipline is rule-governed in a way that survives stress, fatigue, betrayal, and even possession.

This is a defense in the technical sense: it is the structural protection against the recognition that he is, at the level of capacity, a wielder of disproportionate force. The discipline permits him to act without admitting what he is. **Without the discipline he would have to acknowledge that he holds the power of a small god; with the discipline he can continue to think of himself as a man with a job.** The cost of failure is high — when the discipline slips (rare, but it has, under Zadkiel-level provocation), the actions taken are not recoverable, and Blaze's post-hoc shame about them is the truest grief he displays.

---

## IV. THE COMPENSATORY UPPER STRUCTURE

Beyond the defenses proper, Blaze has built a small set of compensatory practices that function as scaffolding around the wounded structure. These are not defenses in the strict sense; they are habits, rituals, and chosen frames that hold the system together.

- **The bike as ritual object.** Maintained personally, never delegated. Mechanical work on the bike is the closest thing to meditative practice he undertakes. The activity displaces intrusive content, restores a sense of competent agency, and connects him longitudinally to his father's profession and Crash's tutelage — a permitted form of grief-work disguised as chores.

- **The road as church.** He does not enter conventional churches except under operational necessity. The road serves the equivalent function: a place of solitude, a place where the conditions of his life are taken seriously by the landscape, a place where the moral work occurs.

- **Diner culture as social minimum.** Counter seating, brief exchanges with waitstaff, payment in cash, modest tips that exceed expectation by enough to be remembered. This is **the floor of his social life** — the minimum interaction with strangers required to keep him from full isolation, conducted in a setting where exit is always available within minutes.

- **The leather jacket and the boots as armor.** Worn across decades with minor variation. Functions as a uniform — externalizes the role, removes the daily decision-cost of self-presentation, and provides a small physical layer between his skin and the world that the transformation cannot fully take from him because it precedes the transformation in his self-image.

- **Cash, paper maps, analog tools.** A persistent low-tech preference. Functions defensively against the surveillance and tracking he intuits (correctly) is constant, but also functions psychologically as **a refusal to be embedded in the systems of the present**, which would require accepting a future he does not believe he will have.

- **Naming small acts of kindness as the work.** When asked what he does, he describes the smallest available action — *I helped a guy with a flat, I gave a kid a ride home* — rather than the cosmic-scale work. This is a deliberate framing: the small acts are what he can survive thinking about. The cosmic work is what the Rider does.

---

## V. FAILURE MODES

A defensive architecture this elaborate has predictable failure points. The file enumerates them as operational intelligence.

- **The split collapses under extreme provocation involving a child harmed.** Pronoun integration occurs; the Rider becomes "I"; the targeting discipline frays at the edges. Recovery to baseline takes days.

- **Counterdependence fails when Roxanne or his son is in play.** He asks. He accepts help. The post-hoc shame at having asked produces a withdrawal episode of one to three weeks.

- **Asceticism inverts catastrophically when a pleasure is forced on him by circumstance** (offered hospitality he cannot refuse without insult, a celebration he is dragged into, a gift). He becomes more taciturn than usual, drinks more that night, and departs within twenty-four hours.

- **Sublimation degrades into compulsion in periods without operational targets.** Idleness is the most dangerous condition for him. A surveillance team would observe escalating restlessness, drinking, and the manufactured seeking-out of incidents that would not, in better-regulated periods, rise to his attention.

- **Theological intellectualization collapses around intimate losses,** producing the rare depressive episodes deep enough to incapacitate him for weeks. The Aaron-era loss of the son is the type case.

- **Sarcasm inverts to plain declaration under genuine stakes.** Allies who know him learn that the moment the irony drops, he is no longer protecting himself, and the situation has moved past what the defenses can hold.

---

## VI. INTEGRATED ASSESSMENT

The architecture is **unusually mature for the trauma load.** A subject with Blaze's developmental history (two pre-adolescent parental losses, conditional foster attachment, adolescent catastrophic bargain, six decades of somatic-supernatural retraumatization) would, in the general case, present with primitive defenses dominant — pervasive splitting, projective identification leaking into interpersonal relationships, somatic delegation of all distress, and a moral compass either collapsed into nihilism or hypertrophied into rigid cruelty. Blaze has, against these odds, organized a system in which the primitive defenses are *contained and operationalized* — the splitting targets a single, externally-validated container; the somatic dissociation is bounded by an asymmetric force-discipline; the counterdependence is offset by an intact sublimation toward the protection of strangers — and the higher-order defenses (sublimation, repetition worked toward mastery, moral discipline) are robust enough to do most of the daily work.

The defensive system's cost is the man's life. He has paid for the architecture with every personal good — wife, child, home, body, sleep, taste, pleasure, futurity — he might have accumulated. **He is, in defensive terms, a structurally well-built ruin.** The file's conclusion: the defenses are not the problem. The defenses are what has kept him useful, moral, and alive. The problem is the foundation they rest on, which is the unmetabolized seventeen-year-old conviction that he is the author of his own damnation and owes every subsequent day as restitution. Until that conviction is touched, the architecture will hold, and the man inside it will continue to be largely inaccessible — to allies, to lovers, to himself.

— UATU, file continues.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE — JOHN BLAZE

*Decade-by-decade clinical evolution. Frameworks: attachment theory (Bowlby/Main), structural dissociation (Van der Hart/Nijenhuis), affect-regulation (Schore/Porges), cognitive schema (Young), self-discrepancy (Higgins), and the trauma-developmental model (Herman, van der Kolk). Each decade is anchored in cited behavior, with attention to what changes, what calcifies, and what migrates from one defensive register to another.*

---

## I. THE PRE-TRANSFORMATION DECADE (Childhood–c.1972 / *Marvel Spotlight* #5 substrate)

**Affect regulation.** What can be reconstructed from the carnival flashbacks (*Spotlight* #5; *Ghost Rider* vol.2 #1 retrospective; Aaron, *Ghost Rider* #28) is a child with bimodal affect: a public register that is performative-bright (the stunt-show smile, the showmanship he learned by mimicry of Barton and Crash) and a private register that is muted-watchful. The Simpson home is depicted as warm but conditional — affection is bundled with the imperative to ride, perform, and not fail. This is the substrate for the lifelong inability to occupy a mid-register affect. The child learns to perform "happy" on cue and to swallow grief silently; he does not learn the unremarkable middle.

**Cognitive style.** Concrete-operational, kinesthetic, mechanically literate. Blaze's intelligence — and it is real — develops in the medium of motor skills, throttle control, ramp geometry, and bike maintenance. He thinks with his hands. The verbal-abstract channel is comparatively starved; this is not deficit but specialization, and it will haunt him in every later confrontation with theological abstraction.

**Self-concept.** Two foundational discrepancies install themselves in this decade. (a) **Actual-self vs. ideal-self** is defined by Barton Blaze, dead. The ideal is unreachable because it is a ghost. (b) **Actual-self vs. ought-self** is defined by Crash, whose ought is "be brave enough not to need anyone." Both discrepancies, per Higgins, predict (a) dejection-related affect (sadness, disappointment) and (b) agitation-related affect (anxiety, restlessness). Blaze will display both for the rest of his life.

**Attachment substrate.** The mother's disappearance — unexplained to the child, never adequately metabolized — is the load-bearing wound. Bowlbian protest → despair → detachment is truncated at despair; he never reaches healthy detachment because no one helps him narrativize the loss. The result is the **disorganized-avoidant** template: he will want closeness and pre-emptively close it off.

---

## II. THE 1970s — INITIATION AND ACUTE PHASE (*Marvel Spotlight* #5 through *Ghost Rider* vol.2 c.#35)

**Affect regulation.** This decade is the acute traumatic phase, and the affective signature is **alternation between numbing and intrusion** in the classical PTSD pattern (Horowitz's biphasic model). Issues from this period (Friedrich, Isabella) show Blaze cycling between flat-stunned silence (after Crash's death, after each Roxanne separation) and explosive somatic-affective dysregulation (the transformation itself, which is — psychodynamically — affect that has exceeded the container and broken through the skin). There is no integrated middle. He weeps rarely on-panel; when he does, it is private, often on a roadside, posture collapsed over the handlebars.

**Cognitive style.** Magical-bargaining cognition is at its peak. The Faustian act is the cardinal expression: a teenager attempts to negotiate with metaphysics using the only currency he has. Throughout the 70s, his cognition remains transactional — "if I do X, the curse will lift" — and he tries variant after variant (exorcism, prayer, geographic flight, separation from Roxanne for her safety). The cognition is not stupid; it is *developmentally appropriate to the age at which the trauma occurred* and frozen there. Piaget would note the absence of formal-operational acceptance that some systems are not negotiable.

**Self-concept.** This is the decade in which **"I am damned"** is installed as a core schema (Young: Defectiveness/Shame + Punitiveness + Mistrust/Abuse, in combination). It is not yet the calm, load-bearing belief it will become; it is raw, contested, fought against. He still seeks redemption actively. He still believes — with diminishing conviction — that the curse can be lifted by sufficient effort. Late in the decade, beginning roughly with the suicidal subtext of vol.2 #9 and #20, the schema begins to shift from "I must escape this" to "I cannot escape this," which is the precondition for the later anhedonic acceptance.

**Defenses.** Primitive and unintegrated. Splitting (the Rider as "it") begins immediately but is unstable — he sometimes claims authorship of the violence, sometimes disclaims it, sometimes loses memory of it entirely. The dissociative architecture is in flux. Repression is heavy and inefficient; intrusive material breaks through nightly.

**Interpersonal.** Roxanne is the test case. Approach-avoidance is at maximum amplitude in this decade — long courtships, sudden ruptures, returns. The pattern is not yet stylized into the later, quieter withdrawal; it is florid, sometimes melodramatic, frequently tearful.

---

## III. THE LATE 1970s–EARLY 1980s — CALCIFICATION (*Ghost Rider* vol.2 c.#36 through #81)

**Affect regulation.** The acute oscillations begin to **flatten into chronic dysthymia**. The numbing wins more often than the intrusion. Where the early-70s Blaze wept, the early-80s Blaze stares. Bar scenes proliferate; the anesthetic drinking pattern is now visibly established. The transformations remain explosive but the civilian affect compresses toward a baseline of **melancholic constriction with intermittent irritability** — the somatic signature of long-term cortisol load and sympathetic-dominant autonomic tone (Porges: the polyvagal "shutdown" state increasingly dominates over the "mobilization" state, except when the Rider mobilizes for him).

**Cognitive style.** Magical bargaining yields to **practical fatalism**. He stops looking for a global solution and starts looking for a next mile. The cognitive horizon contracts to the operational present, which is, paradoxically, adaptive — it permits function — and pathological — it forecloses planning, savings, futurity. Schema-level, the Defectiveness schema is now welded to an Abandonment/Instability schema: he will not invest in any structure (home, marriage, address) because structures collapse.

**Self-concept.** The Isabella-era apparent separation from Zarathos (#81) is psychologically revealing in what it does *not* produce: relief. Blaze without the Rider, in this brief window, is not happy. The damnation schema is by now structural; the absence of the demon does not lift it because the schema has migrated from the Rider to the self. This is the decisive shift of the period: the curse becomes *him,* not something done to him. Therefore even its removal cannot redeem him.

---

## IV. THE LATE 1980s–EARLY 1990s — DORMANCY AND RETURN (Ketch era; Blaze offstage, then Mackie return)

**Affect regulation.** Offstage years are inferable from the affect of the returned Blaze: harder, terser, with a more efficient anger. The decade of relative quiet did not heal him; it sedimented him. When he reappears with the hellfire shotgun, the affective range has narrowed further. Joy has effectively disappeared from his repertoire. What remains is grim functional baseline + tactical fury. The middle band is gone.

**Cognitive style.** Operational, weapons-forward, mission-discrete. He thinks in terms of present targets and immediate threats. The theological cognition that animated the 70s is mostly retired — he no longer asks *why,* he asks *who needs stopping.* This is, in trauma terms, **the third phase of the structural-dissociation model:** the Apparently Normal Part has hardened around a fixed identity ("the guy who handles this") while the Emotional Parts (the grief over Crash, the love for Roxanne, the abandoned child) are increasingly walled off and rarely accessible.

**Self-concept.** The brother-revelation (Ketch as Dan) and the familial-rage dynamic surface a previously hidden schema: **sibling-displacement and ungrieved childhood.** Blaze's reaction to Ketch is disproportionate to the facts presented, which is diagnostic — the disproportion is the leakage of the never-processed loss of childhood itself. He resents Ketch the way a man resents a younger sibling who got the years of childhood he didn't.

**Defenses.** Splitting is now stylized and efficient. The Rider is referred to consistently in the third person, with a craftsman's vocabulary ("when *he* takes over," "what *it* did"). Dissociation has matured from chaotic to organized — the system works, even as it costs.

---

## V. THE LATE 1990s–EARLY 2000s — INTERREGNUM AND ATTRITION

**Affect regulation.** This is the period of deepest **anhedonic asceticism**. Bar scenes are at their most solitary. Civilian relationships are vestigial. The autonomic profile, inferable from posture and pacing across the period's appearances, is one of chronic hypoarousal — slow movements, low vocal register, minimal facial display — punctuated by the brief hyperarousal of combat. The Window of Tolerance (Siegel) is narrow: he tolerates only the extremes, having lost facility with the middle.

**Cognitive style.** Increasingly **moral-existentialist** rather than theological. He no longer expects metaphysical resolution. The cognition that survives is the operational ethics of intervention: see harm, intervene, leave. The reasoning is fast, intuitive (Kahneman's System 1, refined by twenty years of repetition into something approaching expertise) — and resistant to System 2 elaboration, because elaboration leads to questions he has decided not to ask.

**Self-concept.** Stable-damned. The schema has become so load-bearing that it now functions as **identity rather than wound**. He is the damned man. The damned man does these things. This is, perversely, organizing — it gives him a self when other selves have failed — and it is the structure that will resist every later attempt to revise it.

---

## VI. THE AARON ERA, MID-2000s — THEOLOGICAL RUPTURE AND DISILLUSION (*Ghost Rider* 2006–2009)

**Affect regulation.** Aaron writes Blaze drinking in a roadside dive in #20 — the establishing posture for the era. Affect: flat, dry, sardonic. The melancholy is now lined with **gallows humor**, a development. Where 1970s Blaze wept and 1990s Blaze raged, Aaron-era Blaze deflects with mordant terseness. This is not health; it is the affective signature of a man for whom even despair has become familiar enough to be wry about. Clinically: the depressive baseline is now ego-syntonic, which makes it harder to treat and easier to live with.

**Cognitive style.** The Zadkiel revelation forces a brief reactivation of theological cognition — Blaze must, against his preference, think about Heaven again. He does so badly, in the sense that he does so practically: Heaven lied, therefore Heaven is an enemy, therefore Heaven is to be fought. He does not theorize; he targets. This is the cognitive style that will define him going forward: **theological grievance executed as operational opposition.** He believes in good and evil; he distrusts every institution claiming jurisdiction.

**Self-concept.** Critical event: the revelation that he was *chosen* from the womb. This should, in a healthy system, partially relieve the damnation schema (he is not random refuse; he is conscripted). Instead it inflames it. **Reaction-formation against grandiosity** is now diagnostic: any frame that elevates him is resisted, sabotaged, refused. The deep belief — "if I am chosen, I have been used; if I have been used, I am still not free; therefore the chosen-ness is another collar" — preserves the damnation schema by reframing election as exploitation. The schema is now multiply-defended.

**Defenses.** Splitting matures into something approaching **negotiated co-presence**. He and the Rider are, by the end of Aaron's run and into *Fear Itself: The Fearless,* more integrated than at any prior point — he can speak with it, sometimes through it. But integration is partial; the disowned material (his own appetite for punishment, his own rage) remains assigned to the Spirit. The split is now functional rather than chaotic, which is progress, but it is not resolution.

---

## VII. THE 2010s — FAMILIAL ANNIHILATION AND CONTAINMENT FAILURE

**Affect regulation.** The loss of the Aaron-era family (son, by various continuity routes) returns Blaze to the **acute intrusive phase** briefly, then collapses into a deeper, harder version of the chronic baseline. The affective range now excludes joy categorically. What remains: muted melancholy, sardonic dryness, tactical focus, and the explosive transformation-channel. The somatic markers of long-term traumatic load are pronounced — implied sleep debt, dietary disregard, the body kept barely above functional threshold by the supernatural substrate that has, paradoxically, become his life-support.

**Cognitive style.** **Repetition compulsion** is now visible *to him,* intermittently. He notices, in moments of quiet, that he keeps doing the same thing. The noticing does not stop the doing. Awareness without alteration is one of the cruelest stages of trauma — the patient sees the pattern and lacks the somatic permission to break it.

**Self-concept.** Damned, and now also **bereaved-as-identity.** The losses have stratified: father, mother, foster father, son, the woman, the home, the body, the human face. He carries the losses as a kind of layered armor; each loss confirms the schema, and the schema makes each loss bearable by predicting it. The system is closed.

---

## VIII. THE LATE 2010s–PRESENT — KINGSHIP, AVENGERS, DISSOCIATED COMPLIANCE (Cates *Damnation*; *Avengers* 2018–)

**Affect regulation.** The King-of-Hell tenure is psychologically diagnostic: he occupies the throne with **dissociated compliance**, the affect of a man going through motions he does not believe in, in a role he accepted because refusal seemed disloyal to a cosmic order he no longer respects. The flatness here is not depression in the acute sense — it is **dissociative numbing in service of role-tolerance.** He can do the job because he has stopped attending to himself doing it.

The Avengers tenure shows the same. He quarters himself in the basement. He attends meetings. He executes missions. He does not eat with the team, does not banter, does not accept rooms upstairs. The behavior reads — and Aaron writes it to read — as **active counterdependent withdrawal within proximity,** which is a more advanced and more sustainable form of avoidance than the early-decade pattern of geographic flight. He has learned to be alone in company. This is, by certain metrics, an improvement; by others, a deeper entrenchment.

**Cognitive style.** Operational, terse, expert. His tactical reads are excellent and fast. His character reads — predator vs. victim, lie vs. truth — are unusually accurate, the product of fifty years of repetition under stakes. The cognition that has atrophied is **futurity-cognition**: he does not plan past the next mile, the next mission, the next confrontation. He cannot imagine himself old. He has never been able to.

**Self-concept.** Damned, chosen, used, bereaved, functional, alone. The self-concept has accumulated layers without revising the foundational schema. The remarkable feature of the contemporary Blaze is that, despite the load, **the prosocial moral function has not degraded.** Across every era, including this one, he intervenes for children, for the road-vulnerable, for the powerless. This is the longitudinal datum that argues against a purely deteriorative course. The moral function is preserved because it is the only register in which he experiences himself as authored rather than written-upon.

**Defenses, integrated read.** Splitting (Rider/self) is now stylized to the point of near-craft. Counterdependence is sustained even in apparent integration (basement, saddlebags). Reaction-formation against grandiosity has fossilized into a near-reflex. Anhedonic asceticism is total. Repetition compulsion is visible and unbroken. Sublimation — the conversion of his own unprotected childhood into vigilance for others' — is the single mature defense, and it is the one that has saved him from the worse outcomes (antisocial drift, true psychopathic collapse, completed suicide).

---

## IX. SYNTHETIC LONGITUDINAL ARC

Across six decades the trajectory is not deterioration and not recovery but **calcification with preserved moral function.** The acute, florid suffering of the 1970s gives way, decade by decade, to a more compressed and more sustainable suffering, organized around a stable-damned identity that costs him every personal good and yields, as its single dividend, a consistent capacity to intervene on behalf of strangers.

Affect has narrowed from bimodal-acute to flat-with-explosive-channel. Cognition has narrowed from magical-bargaining to operational-fatalist. Self-concept has migrated from contested-damnation to load-bearing-damnation-as-identity. Defenses have matured from chaotic to stylized. Attachment remains disorganized-avoidant, now executed with the quiet competence of long practice rather than the florid rupture of early adulthood.

The clinical surprise — and it is genuine — is that under this load, **the moral compass has not corroded.** It has, if anything, sharpened. This is the datum that resists the otherwise grim prognosis: a man who has organized his entire psychological economy around the assumption that he is damned, and who nonetheless spends his nights protecting the unprotected, is demonstrating — in the only language he will let himself speak — the proposition he refuses to entertain in words.

He is good. He knows it imperfectly. He refuses to believe it. He has organized his life around the assumption that the evidence of his goodness is itself a debt accruing interest.

The longitudinal record is the slow, granular, six-decade accumulation of that evidence.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — SUBJECT: JOHN BLAZE

**Classificatory framework.** This assessment uses DSM-5-TR criteria as primary scaffolding, supplemented by ICD-11 where the latter's developmental-trauma constructs (notably Complex PTSD) offer better phenomenological fit. Where the subject's pathology interacts with supernatural ontology, I bracket the metaphysical and assess the behavioral and intrapsychic phenomena as they would present to a clinician blind to the cosmology. Diagnoses are derived from longitudinal behavioral evidence across roughly fifty years of documented activity; collateral information is drawn from observed interactions with Simpson, R.; Ketch, D.; Strange, S.; Banner, B.; and assorted clergy and ad-hoc confessors over the period 1972–present.

---

## I. PRIMARY DIAGNOSES

### A. Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (ICD-11 6B41), chronic, severe, with prominent dissociative phenomena

This is the load-bearing diagnosis. ICD-11's CPTSD construct fits Blaze considerably better than DSM-5-TR's PTSD-with-dissociative-subtype because the etiological substrate is developmental and cumulative rather than monotraumatic, and because the three CPTSD-defining "disturbances in self-organization" (DSO) are all florid and stable across decades.

**Criterion A (qualifying exposure).** Met multiply and gratuitously:
- Witness to or proximate experience of the violent death of biological father (Barton Blaze, stunt fatality, subject in latency).
- Maternal abandonment under threat conditions (Naomi Kale flight; the developmental valence of an unexplained disappearance is functionally equivalent to traumatic loss in a child this age).
- Witness to the death of foster-father Crash Simpson in the immediate aftermath of the subject's catastrophic adolescent attempt to prevent it.
- Decades of combat-equivalent violent exposure as both perpetrator and recipient.
- Repeated somatic catastrophe — the transformation itself — which functions as iterative bodily annihilation and would qualify as Criterion A trauma if it happened once to anyone else.
- Multiple soul-extraction and possession events, which have no DSM analog but functionally constitute identity-erasure experiences.

**Re-experiencing (B-criteria).** Documented across runs: nightmares (particularly chronic in the Friedrich and Mantlo material, recurrent in Aaron); transformation-onset states that read as flashback-equivalent intrusions where the past (Crash's death, the bargain) bleeds through present-tense action; somatic re-experiencing in the form of involuntary skull-substitution at threat cues. In bar scenes across the Mackie run he repeatedly stares at middle distance during conversation in a manner the clinician would code as dissociative re-immersion.

**Avoidance (C-criteria).** The entire geographic biography is avoidance behavior. He does not stay anywhere. He does not keep possessions beyond what fits in saddlebags. He does not maintain correspondence. He refuses to discuss the bargain even with intimates who have earned standing to ask.

**Negative alterations in cognition and mood (D-criteria).** Persistent and exaggerated negative beliefs about self ("I am damned" — fixed, treatment-resistant); persistent distorted blame of self for the deaths of Crash and others; markedly diminished interest in activities (including activities, like riding, that should constitute mastery pleasure); feelings of detachment from others (operationally constant); persistent inability to experience positive emotions (anhedonia foregrounded by Aaron, Cates, and Brisson independently).

**Arousal and reactivity (E-criteria).** Hypervigilance in civilian settings (he scans rooms on entry — depicted across writers); exaggerated startle to specific cues (children's distress, the smell of gasoline burning, ecclesiastical authority); irritability and verbal aggression toward authority figures; reckless and self-destructive behavior (the entire vocational profile).

**CPTSD-specific DSO clusters:**
1. *Affect dysregulation.* Constricted baseline with explosive breakthrough; no functional mid-register. Self-soothing achieved exclusively via alcohol, motion (riding), or violence-with-righteous-frame.
2. *Negative self-concept.* "Damned" as identity-level conviction, not merely affect. The self-concept survives intact through evidence that should disconfirm it (canonization-equivalent appointments by Heaven, expressions of love by Roxanne, demonstrations of moral excellence acknowledged by Doctor Strange).
3. *Disturbances in relationships.* Chronic avoidance of closeness; serial pre-emptive abandonment; inability to sustain dyadic intimacy across time despite preserved capacity for acute-crisis loyalty.

**Course.** Continuous since the 1972 baseline. No documented remission periods exceeding weeks. Brief stabilizations during periods of de-cursing (issue #81, Aaron's brief depowering arc) reveal the underlying CPTSD persisting unchanged when the supernatural overlay is subtracted — clinically diagnostic, as it confirms the psychiatric pathology is not merely an artifact of the curse.

**Dissociative specifier.** Strongly warranted. Depersonalization (he describes his own skull-state as observed from outside), derealization (post-transformation reorientation periods), and what would clinically present as identity-alteration episodes (the Rider as third-person agent) all meet threshold.

### B. Major Depressive Disorder, Recurrent, Severe, with Melancholic Features (DSM-5-TR 296.33)

Distinct from and comorbid with the CPTSD, not subsumed by it. Discrete major depressive episodes are documentable across eras, characterized by:

- Persistent anhedonia exceeding what affective numbing alone would predict; no demonstrated capacity for sustained pleasure across the entire documentary period.
- Diurnal mood variation with worsening in early morning hours (the canonical "he is alone in a roadside diner at 4 a.m." beat that recurs across writers).
- Early-morning awakening; terminal insomnia distinct from PTSD-attributable middle insomnia.
- Psychomotor constraint rather than agitation — slowed speech, economy of gesture, prolonged stillness.
- Excessive and inappropriate guilt of near-delusional intensity (the damnation belief functions as mood-congruent quasi-delusional content during severe episodes).
- Recurrent suicidal ideation, both passive (the long-running pattern of taking damage that should kill him) and at intervals active (Friedrich's Spotlight-era despair scenes; the Mackie-run bar monologues; Aaron *Ghost Rider* #20 opening).

The melancholic specifier is appropriate: the depression has a quality of distinctness from ordinary sadness, is unresponsive to environmental positives, and includes the classic melancholic guilt-tinged self-laceration.

### C. Alcohol Use Disorder, Moderate, in a Functional Pattern (DSM-5-TR 303.90)

Four to five criteria met across the documentary period:
- Drinking in larger amounts and over longer periods than intended (depicted bar scenes).
- Persistent desire to cut down inferable from intermittent abstinence periods that fail.
- Continued use despite knowledge of physical and psychological consequences.
- Tolerance — Blaze functions on quantities that would incapacitate civilian drinkers.
- Use in physically hazardous situations (operating a motorcycle, engaging in combat).

The pattern is anesthetic and solitary rather than social or recreational, which has prognostic and characterological significance: the alcohol is doing labor the subject cannot do otherwise. It is not addictive in the dopaminergic-reward sense so much as it is *functionally palliative*. Were he to lose access to it, the underlying depressive and anxious phenomena would surface rather than be replaced by withdrawal craving.

### D. Persistent Insomnia Disorder (DSM-5-TR 780.52)

Independently diagnosable. Pre-dates and post-dates specific PTSD-related sleep disturbance. Chronic, unresponsive to environmental modification, with documented impairment in daytime functioning that the subject masks via stimulant compensation (caffeine, nicotine, the arousal generated by riding).

---

## II. SUBTHRESHOLD AND PROVISIONAL CONSIDERATIONS

### Prolonged Grief Disorder (DSM-5-TR 309.89), provisional

The losses of Crash Simpson, his son, and serially of Roxanne Simpson produce grief reactions that have not metabolized across decades. The criterion of yearning and preoccupation is harder to assess because Blaze's avoidance defenses suppress overt grief expression, but the behavioral residue — the repetition-compulsion staging of Crash's death scene with himself in both roles — is consistent with unresolved grief structuring the entire vocational identity.

### Acquired Conversion / Functional Neurological Symptoms

Bracketing the supernatural, certain transformation-onset patterns (involuntary, threat-cued, ego-dystonic in early continuity) would warrant FND consideration in a non-cursed subject. In the actual cosmology this is moot; noted for completeness because it illuminates the *form* the curse takes — it expresses itself through the symptomatic vocabulary the subject's psyche was already organized to speak.

### Moral Injury (non-DSM construct, military psychiatry literature)

Highly applicable. The subject has perpetrated, witnessed, and failed to prevent acts that violate his moral code, repeatedly, across decades, often under conditions of deception by superordinate authorities (Mephisto, Zadkiel). Moral injury is distinct from PTSD in that its core affect is shame and self-condemnation rather than fear, and its self-concept disturbance is moral rather than safety-oriented. Blaze's "I am damned" belief is better characterized as moral-injury cognition than as PTSD-criterion D negative self-belief; the latter framing under-specifies it.

---

## III. COMORBIDITY STRUCTURE

The diagnoses are not independent. The CPTSD substrate generates the depressive episodes (depression as the affective consequence of fixed negative self-cognition and chronic interpersonal isolation); the depression and CPTSD jointly drive the alcohol use (palliation of intrusive symptoms and anhedonic baseline); the alcohol use and CPTSD jointly produce and sustain the insomnia; the insomnia exacerbates affective dysregulation and intrusive symptoms, closing the loop. Moral injury sits transversally, contributing rigidity to the self-concept that would otherwise be more responsive to corrective experience.

The architecture is self-reinforcing and treatment-resistant by design — every component stabilizes every other. Pharmacological intervention on any single node would predictably fail without simultaneous attention to the others, and the cosmological complication (he is, in fact, partially correct that he is bound to a damnation entity) means standard reality-testing protocols cannot be deployed against the core belief.

---

## IV. DIFFERENTIAL — WHAT THE SUBJECT IS NOT

A rigorous differential is essential because surface presentation invites several misdiagnoses, each of which would mis-route intervention.

### Not Dissociative Identity Disorder (DSM-5-TR 300.14)

Surface presentation strongly suggests DID: a second named agent with distinct affect, capabilities, and apparent agency; periods of host amnesia (pre-Aaron); third-person self-reference. The differential turns on etiology and structure. DID alters are developmentally formed from dissociated self-states in response to early trauma without external entity. Zarathos is canonically an exogenous entity bonded by metaphysical contract, not a developmentally-generated alter. *However* — and this is clinically important — Blaze's psychological *use* of the Rider exhibits DID-adjacent functional architecture. He has organized his disowned aggressive and sadistic registers into the Rider-container, exploiting the supernatural fact to perform the developmental work an actual DID alter would perform. The diagnosis is wrong; the dynamic it points at is real.

### Not Antisocial Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.7)

The violence profile invites the question; the structure refutes it. ASPD requires pervasive disregard for the rights of others, deceitfulness, impulsivity, irritability, reckless disregard for the safety of self or others, irresponsibility, and lack of remorse, with onset before age 15 and conduct disorder history. Blaze fails on virtually every count: his violence is rule-governed and asymmetric, targeting only those whose own conduct meets internal predator-criteria; his honesty within personal relationships is, if anything, pathologically uncompromising; his recklessness is directed at self rather than others; his remorse is hypertrophied to the point of structuring his self-concept. He has a robust, possibly pathological, conscience. ASPD ruled out definitively.

### Not Borderline Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.83)

Affective lability is present, but the BPD criterion set fails on closer examination. Splitting is targeted at a single object (self vs. Rider) rather than diffuse across interpersonal relationships. Identity disturbance is the wrong shape — BPD identity disturbance is chaotic and shifting; his is rigidly fixed at "damned." Fear of abandonment is replaced by expectation of and pre-emption of abandonment, a phenomenologically different organization (avoidant rather than borderline in its interpersonal grammar). No documented suicidal gesture pattern of the manipulative-communicative type characteristic of BPD; the suicidality is melancholic and private. Impulsivity is selective rather than pervasive. Rule out.

### Not Narcissistic Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.81)

Surface power, world-altering capability, and a quasi-messianic role description might suggest grandiose NPD. The presentation is the opposite: persistent reaction-formation against grandiosity, refusal of offered authority (the Kingship of Hell occupied with depressive resignation rather than narcissistic investment), genuine other-orientation in moral action, and absence of the diagnostic vulnerability to narcissistic injury (criticism does not destabilize him because he agrees with it pre-emptively). Vulnerable NPD is closer but still wrong — vulnerable narcissists harbor grandiose fantasies that compensate the depleted self; Blaze does not. He believes the negative self-evaluation. Rule out.

### Not Schizoid Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.20)

Social withdrawal is present, but SPD requires a constitutional indifference to relationships and a flat affective experience of others. Blaze wants closeness, grieves its absence, attaches deeply when permitted, and shows preserved capacity for warmth in narrow conditions (children, the genuinely powerless, occasional comrades who breach his perimeter). His isolation is *defended* rather than *desired*. Rule out.

### Not Avoidant Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.82)

Closer, and a tempting diagnosis. AvPD's hallmark — desire for connection inhibited by fear of rejection — has surface resemblance. The differential turns on what is feared. AvPD subjects fear social humiliation and negative evaluation; Blaze does not. He fears *causing harm to those he attaches to*, a phenomenologically distinct anxiety with a different action repertoire. He does not avoid because he expects to be judged; he avoids because he expects to be the agent of damage. This is more consistent with the CPTSD interpersonal-disturbance criterion than with a discrete personality disorder.

### Not Schizophrenia, Schizoaffective Disorder, or any Primary Psychotic Disorder

Despite the externalized voice (the Rider), the visions, the theological certainties, and the contact with entities other people do not see — none of this is psychotic. The phenomena are real within the cosmology, his reality-testing of the ordinary world is intact, his thought form is organized, his affect is appropriate to content, and the "delusional" belief of damnation is in fact accurate to his metaphysical situation. He passes every reality-testing probe a clinician could administer. Rule out, and note that the differential is *easy* — Blaze's epistemic style is the precise opposite of psychotic: empirical, suspicious, and resistant to numinous claims.

### Not Bipolar Disorder, any subtype

No documented manic or hypomanic episodes. The "switching" between baseline and transformed states is not mood-cycling — there is no euphoria, no grandiose ideation, no decreased need for sleep generated *by* mood elevation (his sleep deficit is depressive and PTSD-driven), no pressured speech, no goal-directed activity surge in the manic sense. Affective range is constrained downward, not oscillating across a wide range. Rule out.

### Not Substance-Induced Mood or Anxiety Disorder

Although alcohol use is significant, the depressive and anxious phenomena predate and persist through periods of relative abstinence, and the temporal sequencing (trauma → mood/anxiety → drinking) is the reverse of what a substance-induced diagnosis requires. The alcohol is consequence, not cause.

### Not Adjustment Disorder

The reaction is not proportionate to a specific identifiable stressor within a three-month onset window. It is lifelong, multi-event, and developmentally rooted. Rule out as inadequate to the chronicity.

---

## V. ETIOLOGICAL FORMULATION

The diagnoses arise from a developmentally legible sequence. Two pre-adolescent attachment ruptures (paternal death, maternal disappearance) establish the substrate of expected loss. Foster placement with the Simpson family installs the conditional contingency: love is available, but it is bundled with the demand to perform escalating risk publicly. The subject metabolizes this as the operative model of love-maintenance. The adolescent crisis — Crash's diagnosis — activates the only coping schema available, "perform impossible risk to keep the family intact," and the supernatural marketplace offers a transaction that fits this schema exactly. The bargain is made under conditions that no consent framework would honor (minor, acute grief, asymmetric information, fraudulent counterparty). The counterparty defrauds him; the foster-father dies anyway; the subject is bonded to a punishment-entity. The remainder of the life is the working-out of this sequence under conditions where escape is structurally impossible.

The diagnoses, in this light, are not pathology so much as predictable cost. The remarkable clinical fact is not that he is symptomatic but that the moral function is preserved — that fifty years of this load have produced a man who is depressively organized, traumatically structured, and chemically self-medicating, but who has not become cruel, has not become indifferent, and has not become the thing he hosts. That preservation is the diagnostic anomaly worth flagging, and it is what distinguishes assessment of this subject from assessment of others with comparable trauma loads who have collapsed into the predicted endpoints.

---

## VI. PROGNOSIS AND TREATMENT CONSIDERATIONS

Prognosis under standard intervention: poor. The conditions sustaining the pathology are not removable through clinical means; the bonded entity is real, the cosmological grievance is justified, and the avoidance pattern is reinforced by genuine danger to attached others. Trauma-focused cognitive-behavioral interventions would fail against a self-concept that is partly accurate. EMDR would have nothing to reconsolidate that has not already been reconsolidated into the existing belief structure dozens of times. Pharmacology would address symptoms while leaving the architecture intact.

The only intervention model with non-trivial probability of partial benefit is one that does not attempt to dismantle the damnation belief but works adjacent to it: harm-reduction on the alcohol, sleep stabilization, and the slow construction of permitted-relationships that do not require him to relinquish the self-concept to maintain them. The Avengers-era basement quartering, read sympathetically, is something like this — a containment that asks nothing of him and offers proximity without demand. It is the closest thing to a therapeutic environment he has ever inhabited, and it works to the limited extent it does precisely because nobody asks him to be other than what he is.

The clinician's final note: the subject is not awaiting rescue. He is awaiting permission to keep doing the work he has organized his life around, with marginally less self-laceration. The realistic clinical goal is to reduce the interest accruing on a debt he will continue to believe he owes.


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: JOHN "JOHNNY" BLAZE

*Catalog of observable tells, micro-patterns, and decision habits across all documented affective and situational states. Compiled from longitudinal review (1972–present). Where a behavior is era-specific, it is so marked; where it is stable across writers and decades, it is flagged as PHENOTYPIC.*

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM STATE

The calm Blaze is rare enough that it constitutes its own diagnostic finding. True calm is observed approximately in the early-morning hours, alone, on a moving vehicle, on open road, weather permitting, no civilians within visual range. Outside of that narrow envelope, what reads as "calm" is in fact **low-amplitude vigilance** maintained at a metabolic cost.

**Postural signature (PHENOTYPIC).** Shoulders slightly forward, weight distributed toward the balls of the feet even when seated, hands rarely fully relaxed — fingers curl into a loose half-fist at rest, thumb tucked across the knuckles in a way consistent with a man who has been struck in the face often and learned to keep his hands ready without telegraphing it. He does not lean back into chairs. He sits with his spine off the backrest, an inch of air behind him.

**Eye behavior.** Sweeps the room on entry — door, exits, persons, hands of persons, then the ceiling (a tell from years of supernatural threat coming from above and behind). Settles on a vantage with sightlines to the entrance. Does not make sustained eye contact in conversation; looks at the speaker's mouth or hairline, glances away at intervals of three to five seconds. The avoidance is not shy; it is hygienic — he does not want to be read and is reluctant to read others he is not actively assessing.

**Verbal baseline.** Sparse. Sentence length short, declarative. Contractions used; profanity used sparingly and almost always directed at situations, not persons. Voice is mid-range, dry, slightly hoarse — consistent with chronic dehydration, alcohol, and the throat damage implied by transformation. He speaks in a flat Midwestern-inflected affect that has been geographically homogenized by decades on the road; regional markers are minimized.

**Micro-tells of calm-state Blaze:**
- Will accept a cup of coffee but rarely finish it; sets it down, forgets it, picks it back up cold. The taking is social compliance; the not-drinking is the actual preference.
- Cleans gear without being asked — bike, sidearm in the Mackie-era continuity, gauntlets. The cleaning is meditative; he does it slowly, with the affect of a man who is using his hands to keep his mind from going elsewhere.
- Hums or whistles fragments — almost always classic country, occasionally early rock — when he believes no one is listening. Stops immediately if he notices an observer.
- Eats standing up when possible. When seated to eat, finishes faster than the group and excuses himself with a head-nod rather than words.
- Sleeps in his clothes. Boots within arm's reach. This is observed across every era and is the single most reliable behavioral marker.

**Decision habit in calm.** Defers low-stakes decisions to others (where to eat, what route to take when a passenger is along, who sits where) with apparent indifference that is actually a strategy of conserving decisional energy for higher-stakes domains. He does not have preferences he will defend below a certain threshold of consequence.

---

## II. MILD STRESS

*Operational definition: noise, crowds, unwanted social demand, civilian friction, mild institutional pressure (paperwork, debriefs, being asked to stay somewhere).*

**Withdrawal cascade.** First sign: he stops humming. Second: hands go into pockets or onto a belt — a gesture that looks casual but removes them from the social field and stages them near where weapons or transformation triggers would be drawn. Third: he finds a wall to put his back to. Fourth: he leaves the room on a pretext — checking the bike, getting air, a cigarette in the eras where he smokes.

**Verbal contraction.** Sentence length drops to four words and under. Responses become monosyllabic. He uses "yeah," "nope," "could be," "we'll see" — a phrasebook of non-commitments that allows the conversation to continue without requiring him to take a position.

**The cigarette / drink / engine ritual.** Under mild stress in any era where the prop is available, he will manufacture a reason to handle something with his hands — light a cigarette, pour a drink, restart the bike, adjust a strap. This is not nicotine craving or thirst; it is **manual self-soothing** of the kind common in chronic-trauma adults who have learned that the body, given a small task, will stop signaling alarm.

**Decision habit under mild stress.** Begins planning his exit. Will not commit to next-day arrangements. Becomes geographically restless: if in a building, moves to a window; if in a vehicle, becomes the driver; if in a town, starts looking at the highway signs.

---

## III. MODERATE STRESS / INTERPERSONAL FRICTION

*Authority figures, perceived condescension, being lectured by gods/angels/well-meaning teammates, romantic pressure, being asked what he wants.*

**Sarcasm activation.** Blaze's wit is sharpest under moderate stress. The dryness curdles into something pointed and economical — usually directed upward (at Doctor Strange, at celestial bureaucrats, at Avengers leadership, at any entity claiming jurisdiction over his soul). The sarcasm is consistent across writers and is one of the few places his intelligence visibly surfaces. He uses it as a substitute for the aggression he is trying not to escalate into.

**Jaw set.** A specific musculoskeletal tell: a slight forward thrust of the lower jaw, lips compressed thin, the masseter visibly working. Repeated by Ploog, Texeira, Saiz, Smith. It precedes a verbal exchange he is about to lose patience with by approximately two to three seconds. Counterparts who learn to read it know they have one more sentence before the conversation ends.

**Physical disengagement.** Will turn his body forty-five degrees off the speaker's axis — not fully away, which would be rude, but enough to break the engagement frame. Cross-armed posture is rare; he prefers thumbs-in-belt, hands-on-hips, or one hand braced against a doorframe.

**Decision habit.** Selects the option that minimizes future obligation, even when it costs him short-term. Will refuse free help, free housing, free anything offered with relational strings. Will accept the same goods if framed as a one-time exchange or owed favor. The bookkeeping is meticulous and exclusively in the direction of owing less.

---

## IV. THREAT / COMBAT-IMMINENT STATE

**The stillness.** Counter-intuitively, his pre-combat behavior is *stillness intensification*, not agitation. The fidget-tells (cigarette handling, gear adjustment) cease. Breathing slows and deepens. He stops blinking at normal frequency. Allies who have served with him describe the moment as "the temperature dropping." This is the integration window — the seconds in which the threshold to transformation is being calibrated.

**Hand placement.** Open palms, lowered, slightly forward of the hips. Not raised — raising the hands telegraphs commitment. Lowered hands look passive but are in the optimal position for either drawing a weapon, mounting the bike, or initiating the transformation gesture (which in most eras involves a downward glance at his own hands as the flame begins).

**Verbal pre-combat.** Either complete silence or a single warning sentence delivered flat — "Walk away," "Last chance," "You don't want this." Warnings are offered to human-grade opponents; never to demons, who do not get warnings. The discrimination is consistent and telling: he extends the courtesy of choice to creatures he still considers capable of it.

**The transformation moment.** When volitional (post-Aaron continuity), Blaze initiates by lowering his head, closing his eyes for approximately one second, and then opening them as the change begins. The micro-ritual is identical across writers who have depicted volitional transformation. When involuntary (Bronze Age, early Mackie), the trigger is heralded by his hands rising involuntarily to his temples or face, as if to hold his skull in place against what is removing it.

**Decision habit in threat.** Triages by vulnerability, not by tactical priority. Will leave a high-value target uncaptured to evacuate a civilian. Will take damage to absorb damage that would otherwise reach a non-combatant. This is consistent enough across six decades to constitute a tactical liability that adversaries who know him can exploit — and several have.

---

## V. ACTIVE COMBAT — RIDER-INTEGRATED

**Targeting hierarchy.** Predators first, by which he means actors currently inflicting harm on the powerless. Demonic entities second. Generic combatants third. Property damage is incidental and uninhibited; he does not care about cars, buildings, or terrain.

**The Penance Stare protocol.** Deployed selectively, not on every opponent. Reserved for actors whose crimes are particularized and against the innocent — abusers, killers of children, traffickers. He does not Stare soldiers, henchmen, or opponents fighting under duress. The discrimination is morally legible and almost juridical: he has an unspoken classification of who has earned which punishment.

**Combat tells:**
- Tilts the skull approximately fifteen degrees when assessing a target — a gesture inherited from the human Blaze's reading of opponents and preserved through transformation.
- Speaks during combat in short sentences delivered at register inappropriate to the flaming skull's anatomy. The voice in Rider state is consistently Blaze's, not a separate timbre. This is canonical and matters — it indicates that the integration is more complete than Blaze admits.
- Uses the chain almost as an extension of vision: trails it, swings it slowly, lets opponents track it, then strikes from an unexpected vector. The fighting style is theatrical in a specific carnival-derived way — he learned to perform under the eyes of paying audiences and has never lost the showmanship.
- Mounts the bike at the latest possible moment in an engagement. Prefers to fight dismounted in close quarters and use the bike for transit and impact strikes. This contradicts a lot of cover art but is consistent in panel-level depiction.

**De-transformation.** Reverts with a slumping of the shoulders, a brief moment of bracing against the nearest stable surface (wall, bike, ground), and a roughly five-to-ten-second period of disorientation during which he is functionally unable to track conversation. Allies have learned to give him this window. Enemies who attack during it have gotten further than expected.

---

## VI. INTIMACY

*The most data-poor domain in the file, by design — Blaze structures his life to minimize the occasions on which intimacy is observable. What follows is drawn from the limited episodes available, primarily with Roxanne Simpson across all eras, with his son in Aaron's run, and in fragmentary moments with Daniel Ketch and a small number of trusted allies.*

**Approach behavior.** Slow, hesitant, marked by extended silences. When seated near a person he is intimate with, he will allow physical proximity (knee-to-knee, shoulder contact) but rarely initiates it. When he does initiate, it is almost always touch to the hands, forearms, or the side of the face — never the torso first, which would commit to embrace. The hand-touch is a careful entry into a domain he no longer trusts himself in.

**The half-sentence.** With intimates, Blaze begins sentences he does not finish — "I wanted to —," "If things were —," "You know I —" — and lets them die. He is not inarticulate; he is editing in real time and concluding that whatever he was going to say will obligate one or both of them in ways he cannot honor. Roxanne, across eras, learns to wait through these and not finish them for him. The ones who finish them for him get the wrong answer.

**Touch quality.** When he does embrace, it is *full* — he commits, holds longer than expected, then breaks sharply rather than gradually. The break is the tell: he cannot taper. Once the embrace ends, he steps back at least a full pace and reasserts the physical distance immediately, as if to demonstrate to himself that he can.

**Verbal intimacy.** He does not say "I love you" easily. When he says it, it is almost always in a context where one of them is about to die or leave. The phrase is functionally a goodbye in his vocabulary. He has been observed to substitute "Be careful," "Don't wait up," "I'll be back," and "Take care of yourself" as equivalents — the latter, delivered without eye contact, is his deepest expression.

**Sexual behavior** is depicted minimally across canon but inferable: monogamous when partnered, abstinent when not, with no observed pattern of casual encounter. The libido is tethered to love-attachment and does not operate independently of it.

**Decision habit in intimacy.** Will sacrifice the relationship to protect the partner from himself. Frames departures as for the other's safety even when the other has explicitly refused that framing. This is the most reliable failure mode in his relational life and the one he has never corrected across fifty years.

---

## VII. GRIEF

**Grief is Blaze's most fluent emotion, but he does not display it the way grief is usually displayed.** There is no weeping in public, almost none in private. There is no breakdown. There is, instead, a deepening of every existing pattern — the silence longer, the drinking heavier, the riding farther, the sleep worse. Grief manifests as **amplification of baseline** rather than disruption of it.

**Acute grief tells (first 48 hours after loss):**
- Will not be in a building. Sleeps outdoors or in motel rooms chosen for proximity to the bike.
- Drinks methodically, not to drunkenness but to anesthesia — paces the intake to maintain a specific sub-clinical numbness.
- Speaks less than usual. Responses to direct questions narrow to nods and head-shakes.
- Refuses food. Will accept water. Will accept coffee. Cigarettes increase markedly in eras where he smokes.
- Visits no one. Calls no one. Will not accept calls. If pursued physically, will move locations.

**Sub-acute grief (one week to several months):**
- Geographic restlessness intensifies. Mileage covered increases substantially.
- Takes more dangerous jobs — accepts hunts and interventions he would normally triage out.
- Damage tolerance increases. Allows injuries that he could have avoided.
- The Rider is summoned more often and with less provocation.
- Conversations with intimates, when forced, focus on practical logistics — what to do with possessions, who needs to be told, how the funeral was — and refuse the affective frame.

**Chronic grief.** Blaze does not appear to fully process loss. The bereavements accumulate in him as strata rather than resolving. He carries Crash, his mother, his father, Roxanne (in iterations), his son, and others as **a population of un-mourned dead** for whom his ongoing life is a kind of restitution. The clinical term is **complicated bereavement**; the operational consequence is that he is always grieving and never visibly grieving, and this is a single continuous state rather than discrete episodes.

**The one tell that breaks containment.** When asked about specific lost persons by someone he trusts, his voice will drop in volume and the response will be slower than his baseline. He will not look at the questioner. He will frequently change the subject by asking a question back. The deflection is a signal, not a refusal — those who recognize it can press once and will sometimes get a single sentence of disclosure before the door closes again.

---

## VIII. VICTORY

*Defined here as: mission successful, innocents preserved, threat neutralized. Not a state Blaze recognizes as victory.*

**Post-mission affect.** Flat. He does not celebrate, does not accept congratulation, does not stay for debriefs longer than required. When others celebrate, he is physically present and emotionally absent — leans on a wall, drinks slowly, exits early.

**The one allowed pleasure.** A long ride immediately following a successful intervention. The ride is solitary, route unplanned, duration determined by fuel and fatigue. This is the closest he comes to reward-seeking, and it is observed consistently across writers and decades. It is also the closest he comes to joy — a muted, motion-derived, weather-dependent contentment that lasts as long as the road does and dissolves on dismount.

**Refusal of credit.** Will deflect to allies, to circumstance, to luck. Will not accept payment in most eras (cash for bounty work is sometimes taken in the Mackie era; almost never elsewhere). Will not be photographed, interviewed, or memorialized. The refusal is reflexive — he does not consider the alternative.

**Decision habit in victory.** Leaves. The successful conclusion of any mission is the trigger for departure, not the trigger for rest. Stable Blaze in a victory state is, paradoxically, the Blaze most likely to disappear for months.

---

## IX. DEFEAT / FAILURE

*Defined as: innocents lost, threat escaped, ally killed, mission compromised.*

**Immediate response.** Flat affect, methodical body-recovery and scene-clearing behavior. He will physically pick up the dead when possible. He will sit with the wounded. He will not speak.

**The internal accounting.** Within hours, Blaze will be reconstructing the engagement in his head, identifying the decision point at which a different choice would have produced a different outcome, and assigning the failure to himself. This is observable in his subsequent dialogue: he uses "I should have" constructions with high frequency in the days following a defeat, and resists when others attempt to redistribute responsibility.

**Behavioral signatures (days to weeks following):**
- Increased combat aggression on subsequent engagements, with reduced strategic patience.
- Acceptance of higher-risk hunts.
- Diminished interest in self-preservation that crosses, periodically, into clearly self-endangering behavior. The Penance Stare is deployed more readily and at higher intensity.
- Drinking patterns shift toward earlier-day initiation.
- Communications with allies thin to operational essentials.

**Long-term metabolization.** A defeat will, eventually, be added to the strata. Blaze does not forgive himself for losses; he carries them. The carrying is constant and is part of why he cannot accumulate goods — every loss becomes a weight against which any new attachment is measured and found too risky.

---

## X. BETRAYAL — SPECIFIC RESPONSE PROFILE

*Treated separately because Blaze's response to betrayal is distinctive and consequential.*

Betrayal by a stranger or enemy produces ordinary combat response. Betrayal by an entity claiming moral or divine authority — the Zadkiel paradigm — produces a categorically different behavioral state: **sustained, methodical, unrelentling pursuit**, prosecuted past the point at which any cost-benefit analysis would terminate it. This is the closest Blaze comes to obsession.

**Tells:**
- Geographic stasis. He will hold position in a region, working a single problem, for periods that contradict his baseline restlessness.
- Information-gathering behavior intensifies. He will speak to sources he would normally avoid, accept alliances he would normally refuse, tolerate institutions he would normally flee.
- Affect deepens into something cold rather than hot — the rage banks rather than burns.
- He becomes more dangerous to bystanders. Discrimination remains intact but tolerance for collateral involvement narrows.

The behavioral state can be sustained for months. It does not relax until the betrayer is reached. It does not relax when the betrayer is killed — it relaxes when the betrayer is *made to understand* what was done. This is the Penance Stare logic extended into a life-strategy.

---

## XI. AUTHORITY — RESPONSE GRADIENT

**To human civilian authority (police, officials, ordinary bureaucrats):** Compliance with minor edge. Provides false names when convenient, true names when pressed. Does not resist arrest in the rare instances he is detained; treats incarceration as a brief inconvenience and exits at the next opportunity.

**To human institutional authority (Avengers leadership, SHIELD-equivalent):** Tactical cooperation, refusal of integration. Will execute lawful directives. Will not attend social functions, will not occupy permanent quarters, will not adopt uniform protocols. The compliance is contractual; the refusal is character.

**To magical authority (Doctor Strange, the Sorcerer Supreme institution):** Wary respect, occasional collaboration, no deference. He will accept tactical guidance from Strange in particular because Strange has earned it over time; he does not extend the courtesy to the office.

**To divine authority (Heaven, angels, celestial bureaucrats):** Active hostility, expressed through sarcasm at low stakes and direct defiance at high stakes. He has been lied to too many times to extend even procedural respect. He will, however, do the right thing when he can identify it independently of the divine instruction — which functionally aligns him with the better angels while denying them credit.

**To infernal authority (Mephisto, demonic hierarchies):** Open contempt, no negotiation, no acceptance of terms. The only exception is strategic — when he holds office in Hell (Cates), he uses the position against itself.

---

## XII. THE ROAD — RITUAL AND ROUTE BEHAVIOR

The road is Blaze's most stable home and his behavior on it is the most patterned dimension of his life.

**Pre-departure ritual.** Walks the bike — visually inspects tires, chain, lights, fuel — before mounting. Touches the gas tank with the flat of his right hand. The touch is unconscious and consistent across artists and decades; it functions as a benediction or a check-in with the machine, and he does not appear to notice he does it.

**Riding posture.** Slight forward lean, elbows soft, weight forward over the front wheel. Helmet use varies by era and is functionally optional in Rider state. He prefers two-lane highways to interstates, back roads to two-lanes, and will route deliberately away from major metropolitan areas when possible.

**Stops.** Diners over chain restaurants. Independent motels over branded hotels. Cash over card in every era where the option exists. Sits with sightlines to the door. Orders simply — eggs, coffee, sandwich. Tips well. Leaves without conversation.

**Mileage.** When in motion-state, regularly covers 400–600 miles per day. When grieving, has been observed to cover over 1,000 in a single push. The mileage is itself a form of self-medication and the upper-end figures correlate with worse internal states.

---

## XIII. SLEEP, SOLITUDE, AND THE SMALL HOURS

**Sleep architecture.** Poor across all eras. Initial onset latency long; he resists sleep, in part because in early continuity sleep onset triggered transformation. The conditioning has persisted past the mechanism. Awakens to small sounds. Does not enter deep sleep with others present unless wounded.

**Nightmare behavior.** Wakes silently — does not cry out, does not thrash — and goes immediately to motion. Will leave the room, walk outside, smoke, or ride. Does not return to bed if the nightmare was severe.

**The 3 AM tell.** Blaze is, statistically, awake at 3 AM. This has been depicted in multiple eras and is operationally significant: he


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS — SUBJECT: JOHN BLAZE

*What a continuous seven-day surveillance package would record, cross-referenced with longitudinal pattern data from every prior monitored interval (1972–present). The subject's life is, despite its supernatural irregularities, profoundly routinized. The routinization is itself a symptom: a man who cannot trust the substrate of his own body imposes structure on every layer above it.*

---

## 1. THE MACRO-RHYTHM: A LIFE ON LOOP

Blaze does not have a week so much as a recurring forty-eight-to-seventy-two-hour cycle that he re-enters with minor variations. The unit is not the calendar week but the *tank of gas*.
