- **Motorcycle operation at the upper ceiling of human capability.** Stunt-trained, decades-practiced, terrain-indifferent. He can ride anything with two wheels and most things with one. He maintains his own machines and can rebuild an engine on the shoulder of a road with hand tools.
- **Improvised mechanical repair generally.** Carnival roustabout skill base: rigging, welding, small-engine work, basic electrical, structural improvisation under time pressure.
- **Firearms.** Hellfire shotgun across the Mackie era and beyond; competent with conventional firearms when supernatural options are unavailable. Marksmanship adequate, not elite; he prefers close work.
- **Hand-to-hand.** No formal style. Brawler with stunt-conditioning, leverage instincts, and a willingness to absorb hits to land one. Effective in the lower weight classes of supernatural combat; outclassed at the cosmic tier and aware of it.
- **Chain work.** The mystic chain in Rider form is wielded with a fluency that implies either intuitive integration with the Spirit's combat memory or genuine practice; either way, operationally seamless.
- **Wilderness and roadside survival.** He sleeps rough by preference. He knows where to find water, where to camp unmolested, which truck stops are safe, which churches will let a stranger sit, which county sheriffs will hassle a man on a bike and which will not. This is enormous tacit knowledge that civilian operators lack.
- **Code-switching across American sub-strata.** He can sit in a biker bar, a Pentecostal church, a tribal council, a hospital waiting room, a county jail, a diner at 4 a.m., and a superhero conference room, and in each be unobtrusive enough to function. The file notes this is unusual; most high-capability subjects are legible only in one or two registers.
- **Children, handling of.** He is good with frightened children specifically. Calm voice, low posture, no sudden movement, willingness to wait. This is a trained competency, refined over decades of being the adult who arrives at the scene where a child needs an adult. It cannot be faked; children detect the fake.

---

## 6.5 RESOURCES, MATERIAL AND NETWORK

**Material footprint, deliberately minimal.** Saddlebags, a bike, a jacket, cash when he has it, no fixed address by preference. The minimalism is itself an asset: nothing to seize, nothing to threaten, nothing to lose that he has not already accepted losing. A subject with no attack surface is hard to coerce.

**The bike as platform.** Functionally a mobile base of operations, mission-capable, indestructible in conjunction with the rider, capable of dimensional transit. No comparable single-asset platform exists in the field inventory.

**Network — thin but high-quality.** Blaze does not maintain a broad social network, but the contacts he has are unusually capable:
- *Stephen Strange.* Operative working relationship; mutual respect; Strange will take his call.
- *Daniel Ketch (brother).* Volatile but real bond; reinforcement available in extremis.
- *Caretaker lineage / mystical support figures.* Institutional knowledge of Spirits of Vengeance lore accessible to him.
- *The Avengers (Aaron-era and after).* Standing teammate status; quarters, equipment, intelligence access available.
- *Other Spirits of Vengeance.* Following his "World Rider" period, network of analogous operators globally; loose but real.
- *Roadside America itself.* Diner waitresses, mechanics, motel clerks, small-town clergy, bartenders — the diffuse civilian network of people who remember him kindly because he intervened once and asked nothing. This is not an organized resource but it is a vast, distributed safe-house network that activates on recognition.

**Reputational asset among adversaries.** Demons, in canon, *know* him. The name carries deterrent weight in the supernatural underworld. Many lower-tier supernatural threats decline to engage on identification. This is force-multiplier intelligence asset: he wins fights he never has to have.

---

## 6.6 RESILIENCE FACTORS — WHY HE IS STILL OPERATIONAL AFTER FIFTY YEARS

This is the analytically interesting question. The file's accumulated trauma load on this subject would, in a baseline human, produce one of three outcomes by year ten: completed suicide, decompensation into psychosis, or moral collapse into the violence he was supposed to be fighting. None of these has occurred. Why.

**1. Externalization of the rage.** Pathological as a defense (see §3), the splitting of aggression into "the Rider" preserves Blaze's self-concept as a man who does not want to hurt anyone. This is technically false but operationally protective. It allows him to wake up the next day still recognizing himself. Subjects who must integrate their own violence into their daytime identity tend to corrode faster.

**2. Mission as scaffold.** Depression in the absence of structure is lethal; depression with a mission is endurable. Blaze always has a mission — the next predator, the next endangered child, the next road. The structure is provided by the world's inexhaustible supply of victims, which is grim but stable. He does not have to find meaning; meaning finds him hourly.

**3. The road as regulation.** Motion is, for him, a nervous-system regulator. Riding is meditative, physically demanding enough to discharge arousal, cognitively engaging enough to interrupt rumination, and solitary enough to permit grief processing without performance. He has, in effect, a daily self-administered somatic therapy that he does not recognize as such. Take away the bike and he decompensates within weeks; leave him the bike and he can carry almost any load.

**4. Moral clarity as anti-nihilism vaccine.** The most dangerous late-stage outcome for chronically traumatized high-capability operators is nihilism — the conclusion that nothing matters and therefore any action is permitted. Blaze is structurally immune. His belief that he is damned implies a moral universe in which damnation is real, which implies that good and evil are real, which implies that his interventions matter. The damnation belief, paradoxically, is what keeps him from becoming what he most fears. He cannot stop believing in stakes.

**5. Absence of self-pity as a habit.** He grieves; he does not complain. The distinction is operationally large. Self-pity recruits an audience and requires energy to maintain; grief is private and metabolizes. Blaze's grieving style — solitary, alcoholic, nocturnal, brief — is unhealthy but efficient. He does not get stuck in the telling.

**6. Tolerance for ambiguity in metaphysical matters.** He does not need the cosmos to make sense. He has been lied to by Heaven and Hell; he files this and continues. Operators who require coherent meta-narratives crack when the narrative breaks. Blaze never had one.

**7. Episodic respite, taken when offered.** He does not refuse all rest. He will sit in a diner for two hours. He will pet a dog. He will let a child show him a drawing. These micro-recoveries are not luxuries; they are the entire recovery architecture, and his willingness to receive them — briefly, without forming attachments — keeps him from total depletion.

**8. The refusal to die.** Despite passive-suicidal accommodation (see §2), Blaze has, in canon, refused multiple offered ends. When offered annihilation as a way out of the curse, he has declined. The motive is not self-preservation in the ordinary sense; it is the belief that if he stops, the next victim does not get an intervener. The conscience prevents the suicide it otherwise would invite. This is a dangerous equilibrium but it has held for fifty years.

**9. Brother, son, lost wife — as anchors even in absence.** The lost objects function as moral north stars. He does not need them present to be oriented by them. Loss has been converted to direction. This is rare; most subjects who have lost what he has lost lose direction with them.

**10. Constitutional capacity for solitude.** He can be alone for long stretches without decompensating. Many high-trauma subjects cannot; the silence becomes intolerable and they recruit chaos. Blaze tolerates his own company. This is partly trained (carnival road life, then fifty years of fugitive existence) and partly constitutive, but either way it is the prerequisite for the sustainable lifestyle he has built.

---

## 6.7 ASSETS HIDDEN INSIDE WHAT LOOK LIKE LIABILITIES

The file flags several attributes that read as pathology but function, in operational context, as advantages:

- **The drinking.** Anesthetic, yes; alcohol use disorder, defensibly. But: it is dose-controlled, time-controlled (nocturnal, post-mission), and has not produced significant operational degradation in five decades. As coping mechanisms among the chronically traumatized go, it is unusually well-contained.
- **The avoidance of intimacy.** Costs him love; saves the people he loves. Every romantic partner he has had has been a target. The avoidance is, among other things, a security protocol he has paid for in blood and learned the hard way.
- **The asceticism.** Reads as self-punishing; functions as minimization of attack surface, low logistics overhead, and immunity to bribery.
- **The expectation of betrayal.** Reads as paranoid; functions as accurate priors. The entities that have repeatedly tried to use him have, in fact, tried to use him. His suspicion is calibrated to his actual environment.
- **The refusal of redemption narratives.** Reads as depressive cognitive distortion; functions as immunity to the manipulation vector most commonly used against him ("you can be free if you just…"). He cannot be sold his own salvation, because he does not believe it is available for sale.
- **The third-person framing of the Rider.** Reads as dissociation; functions as a kind of internal command-and-control architecture, with Blaze as the civilian governor of a weaponized subordinate. The architecture is psychologically costly and operationally effective.

---

## 6.8 THE SUMMARY ENTRY

Strip the supernatural off and what remains is: a physically capable, pain-tolerant, road-trained, hand-skilled, mechanically literate working-class American man with elite threat-perception, an unbreakable moral compass, low ego, high one-shot loyalty, calibrated humility about his own knowledge, an exceptional capacity for solitude, a fully metabolized relationship with his own death, and a depressive organization that has been successfully load-bearing for fifty years without collapse. Add the supernatural — the strength, the hellfire, the chain, the Stare, the bike, the soul-sight, the near-invulnerability, the network of demonic reputational deterrence — and the asset profile becomes one of the most operationally complete in the field inventory.

The deepest entry on the ledger, and the one that everything else rests on: he has been offered every exit, and he has not taken one. Not the deals, not the throne, not the death, not the forgetting, not the redemption. He keeps showing up. Whatever else the file concludes, that fact — the unbroken record of showing up — is the irreducible asset, and the reason this dossier exists at all.


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION — SUBJECT: JOHN BLAZE

---

## 6.0 Prefatory Note on the Shape of His Collapse

Most subjects break by losing function. Blaze breaks by losing **governance over a function that does not stop**. His decompensation is not a descent into incapacity; it is a descent into capacity unmodulated. He does not freeze, panic, dissociate-into-passivity, or psychotically fragment. He **accelerates**, in a phrase used elsewhere in this file: the throttle goes wider, the brake assembly degrades, and the vehicle — bodily, supernatural, moral — continues forward at increasing velocity until something external intervenes or something internal that should not have given way finally does. The clinical interest in Blaze is therefore not "what makes him stop working" but "what makes him stop being able to choose how he works." The latter is the operative question for any agency, ally, or adversary trying to predict him.

What follows is the escalation curve in detail, the specific stressor classes that move him along it, the somatic and behavioral telemetry at each stage, the patterns of breakdown observed across six decades of canon, and the recovery pathways (and their failure rates).

---

## 6.1 The Five-Stage Escalation Curve

Blaze's collapse is **staged, not sudden**, and the stages are observable to a trained eye from the outside. He has been in some of these stages for years at a stretch; he has cycled through all five in a single night (the climax of the Aaron run; the Damnation arc opening; the Crash-Simpson-stunt night in flashback).

### Stage One — *Baseline Constriction* (his "well")

The healthy ceiling for this subject is already below the population mean. Baseline presents as: muted affect, monosyllabic speech, watchful eyes, low-grade vigilance scanning entry/exit of any interior space, hands occupied (cigarette, coffee cup, bottle, throttle, the small unconscious thumb-against-index-knuckle tic visible across artists from Ploog to Smith). Sleep is poor but managed via exhaustion. Drinking is solitary, nocturnal, paced — two to four fingers of whatever brown liquor the bar serves, slowly, over a long sit. He is *functional*, *reliable in a one-shot frame*, and *unavailable for futurity*. **This is not health. This is the equilibrium of a chronically traumatized organism that has stopped trying to climb out.**

### Stage Two — *Loaded Withdrawal* (the warning)

Triggered by accumulation of moderate stressors (see §6.2). Presentation shifts in observable ways: he stops talking almost entirely; he removes himself geographically from group settings — basement quarters, the far booth, the parking lot, the highway shoulder; nightly mileage on the bike increases; alcohol intake increases and the pace tightens (the same volume in less time); cigarette consumption, where present, returns or doubles; he stops eating with others, then stops eating regular meals, then subsists on roadside food consumed standing. He answers direct questions with delay and refuses indirect ones. **He is still in command of the Spirit at this stage, but the threshold for involuntary transformation is lower.** This stage can last days to months; the Mackie-run reintroduction depicts him essentially permanently here.

### Stage Three — *Disinhibited Aggression Within the Rules* (the tightening)

Tactical violence increases in intensity without yet violating the moral code. Predators encountered in the field receive treatment at the upper bound of what he previously considered proportionate. The Penance Stare is administered at full duration where a partial would have sufficed. Property destruction expands. Bystander tolerance for collateral effects narrows. His language with allies becomes flatly contemptuous in a way that is recognizable to anyone who has worked around him before — clipped imperatives, refusal to brief, departures without notice. **He is still distinguishing predator from victim with perfect accuracy** — this is the load-bearing fact that separates this stage from the next — but he is no longer modulating the response within the predator category. The drinking at this stage often pivots from anesthetic to *fuel-equivalent*: he drinks to dull the gap between transformations, then rides.

### Stage Four — *Governance Loss* (the break)

The boundary between Blaze and the Spirit erodes. Third-person reference to the Rider drops out of his speech; first-person plural ("we") appears intermittently and is a hard diagnostic. Transformation triggers expand to include states he previously could suppress through (those who have watched him knew the rituals: the slow exhale, the hand on the bike's tank, the eyes-closed three-count). Memory gaps return even in the Aaron-and-after era when integration had supposedly stabilized. He undertakes pursuits beyond rational cost-benefit — the Zadkiel pursuit across Heaven itself is the type-specimen — and refuses extraction by allies. Sleep collapses entirely. Eating ceases. The body, already not a reliable home, becomes a vehicle he is willing to total. **He stops asking who the target serves and begins targeting the institution.** Doctor Strange's interventions at this stage have a documented success rate that is not high.

### Stage Five — *Identity Collapse / Reabsorption* (the floor)

The rarest and most dangerous stage. Observed in: the Zarathos-undiluted possession episodes (late Bronze Age); the brief de-powered nadir of the Aaron run inverted into the World Rider overcompensation; the King-of-Hell tenure in its most dissociated weeks. Blaze the man becomes functionally inaccessible — present in the body (or skull) but not narratively in command. Affect is flat to absent; speech is ceremonial or absent; recognition of former intimates is impaired or weaponized. **Crucially, the moral compass survives even here**, but its administration is no longer recognizably him: it is colder, more total, and indifferent to context (Roxanne in the room, a child in the line of fire, an ally on the wrong side of a sentence). Recovery from Stage Five has, in every documented case, required an external rupture — usually the proximity of someone he loved before his first parental loss equivalent, or a forced theological intervention. He has never recovered from Stage Five through interior resources alone.

---

## 6.2 Stressor Taxonomy: What Moves Him Up the Curve

Not all stress is equal. Blaze's escalation kinetics depend on the **class** of stressor, not the magnitude.

### Class A — *Acute physical/tactical threat*

Counterintuitively, this barely moves him. Combat, injury, supernatural assault, even bodily destruction of conventional kinds — these are inside his domain. He may move from Stage One to Stage Two for the duration of the engagement and return to Stage One within hours. **A gunfight is, for him, restorative**; it is the rare context in which his somatic state and his role are coherent.

### Class B — *Endangerment of a child or road-vulnerable innocent*

Moves him from any stage to Stage Three within seconds, and Stage Three to Stage Four within minutes if the rescue fails. This is his deepest pressure point and overrides every other commitment — mission discipline, team protocol, prior promise, geographic obligation. **An adversary who places a child in the operational frame has, in effect, opened the gate from whatever stage Blaze was in directly to disinhibition.** Aaron's run uses this repeatedly; Friedrich's earliest issues use it; Cates uses it. It is the most consistent stressor in his record.

### Class C — *Betrayal by an entity claiming legitimate authority*

The Zadkiel class. Moves him to Stage Four and locks him there for the duration of the pursuit, often months or years of subjective continuity. Unlike Class B, which spikes and resolves, Class C produces **sustained, methodical decompensation** — he does not lose function, but his entire function becomes the pursuit, and every other commitment is amputated. Allies are dropped. Geographic patterns collapse to the route of the pursuit. Eating, sleeping, intimacy — all subordinated.

### Class D — *Threat or injury to Roxanne, his son, or the Simpson-family memory*

The most volatile stressor in the file. Moves him from any stage to Stage Four or Five, unpredictably. **The unpredictability is the hazard**: most stressors in this subject's profile have predictable escalation kinetics; this one does not. The lever bypasses his defenses because it activates the unresolved adolescent layer — the substrate beneath the curse — and what surfaces is not the adult Blaze's controlled rage but the seventeen-year-old's untrained terror of losing the last attachment. The Spirit, encountering this terror, has historically taken proportionally more room.

### Class E — *Forced stationarity / institutional containment*

Slow stressor, long fuse. Moves him from Stage One to Stage Two over weeks; Stage Two to Stage Three over months. The Avengers basement period is the case study — there is no acute event, only the accumulated pressure of a role he cannot fit. He erodes the role. He provokes incidents that justify his departure. He is not consciously sabotaging; **he is unable to remain still without metabolizing it as captivity**, and the curse's logic and his trauma's logic agree on this point.

### Class F — *Being praised, called good, named as chosen*

The reaction-formation stressor. Produces a paradoxical regression — typically a snap from Stage One into Stage Two, with the secondary feature of relational withdrawal from the praise-source. He will sometimes engineer an incident that disqualifies him from the praise. This is operationally important: **handlers should not motivate him with esteem or moral validation**. The result is the opposite of what is intended.

### Class G — *Offered alliance or accommodation with Hell, however framed*

He refuses initially, and if pressured, accepts on terms designed to fail. The King-of-Hell tenure is the working example: he occupied the throne with the affect of a man waiting to be deposed, and arranged, by minor and steady non-administration, the conditions of his own removal. Pressuring him toward such alliance moves him quickly to Stage Three and then, if sustained, to Stage Five via dissociation rather than disinhibition — the Hell-adjacent decompensation is **colder** than the field decompensation.

---

## 6.3 Behavioral Telemetry: What Surveillance Sees at Each Stage

For a file of this kind, the granular tells matter. The following are observed across runs and artists with sufficient consistency to treat as **reliable diagnostic signal**.

**Speech.** At Stage One, monosyllabic but responsive. At Stage Two, delay of two to four seconds before response; some questions ignored. At Stage Three, imperatives only; he stops using names. At Stage Four, the third-person Rider drops out, "we" appears, and direct address of allies becomes rare. At Stage Five, ceremonial or absent.

**Hands.** Stage One — occupied, calm, the thumb-knuckle tic at rest. Stage Two — the tic accelerates; the cigarette is lit and not smoked; the glass is held but not raised. Stage Three — hands rest on the bike or the shotgun even in indoor settings where neither is to hand; he reaches for absent objects. Stage Four — hands are open at the sides, palms slightly turned out, a posture that artists across decades have drawn without coordination and that precedes transformation by under a second. Stage Five — irrelevant; he is not predominantly in the body.

**Eyes.** Stage One — watchful, tracking exits. Stage Two — fixed-middle-distance, the thousand-yard register. Stage Three — direct, hard, holding contact past the social norm. Stage Four — the pupils are recorded by close witnesses as *not reflecting light correctly* in low ambient illumination; this is the earliest visible somatic precursor to transformation and predates the flame by seconds. Stage Five — not his.

**Drinking pace.** Stage One — slow, paced, two-to-four-finger sit. Stage Two — same volume, less time. Stage Three — refills before empty, standing. Stage Four — abandoned mid-glass; the bottle accompanies him on the bike, often unopened. Stage Five — irrelevant.

**Bike behavior.** Stage One — daily ride, maintenance attended, routes varied. Stage Two — nightly long rides, no destination, return at dawn or near dawn. Stage Three — the bike is not turned off; he sits on it idling outside locations he is supposed to enter. Stage Four — the bike is part of him in a way it is not at lower stages, and the distinction between his transformation and the bike's transformation collapses. Stage Five — the bike rides without obvious volition.

**Sleep.** Stage One — four to five hours, broken, nightmares. Stage Two — three hours or fewer, often refused. Stage Three — daylight micro-sleeps only. Stage Four — none recorded. Stage Five — irrelevant.

**Eating.** Stage One — roadside, alone, sufficient. Stage Two — declined offers of shared meals, takes coffee instead. Stage Three — coffee only. Stage Four — none. Stage Five — irrelevant.

**Geographic radius.** Stage One — touring, broad. Stage Two — narrows to the corridor between his current location and the precipitating stressor. Stage Three — tightens further; he holds a perimeter around the threat. Stage Four — single-vector pursuit, ignoring obstacles. Stage Five — non-Euclidean; he has, on several documented occasions, traveled between planes of existence without conscious decision.

---

## 6.4 Collapse Morphologies: What His Breakdowns Have Actually Looked Like

Across the record, five distinct collapse morphologies recur. They are not mutually exclusive — a given decompensation may begin in one mode and migrate — but each has its own profile.

### Morphology I — *The Fugue Pursuit*

The most common. Triggered by Class C or Class D stressors. He enters Stage Four and conducts a sustained, methodical hunt that may last weeks of subjective time. Sleep and eating collapse; communication with allies degrades to operational minimum; geographic pattern flattens to the pursuit vector. He returns from these episodes thinner, quieter, more inwardly compressed, with memory of the pursuit but a blunted memory of his own internal states during it. **He does not consider these episodes pathological**; he considers them work. The Zadkiel arc is the type-specimen. Approximate frequency across the record: once per decade, with the qualifier that the entire 1990s read as a single extended episode.

### Morphology II — *The Bar-and-Road Spiral*

Triggered by Class E or Class F stressors, or by the accumulation of failed attempts at settlement. He locates himself in a roadside establishment of low ambition, drinks for hours, rides for hours, sleeps in the saddlebags' equivalent, repeats. This morphology is *slow* and superficially stable — he can hold this pattern for months — but represents Stage Two with a slow drift toward Stage Three. Decompensation announces itself in this morphology not by acute incident but by the **disappearance of variety** in his routes, drinks, and language. The Mackie reintroduction era reads as months in this morphology.

### Morphology III — *The Catastrophic Rescue*

Triggered by Class B. He encounters a child or comparable innocent in danger, jumps stages, and executes a rescue that succeeds tactically while costing him a personal good he had been holding. The Spotlight #5 bargain is the originating event of this morphology and Blaze has been re-enacting it ever since. The recurring beat across writers is that the rescue *works* and that **he loses something for it** — a relationship, a body, a year of his life, a piece of his soul — and accepts the loss as appropriate. This is the morphology that looks most like heroism to outside observers and is, internally, the most thoroughly compulsive.

### Morphology IV — *The Throne-Sit*

Triggered by Class G. He accepts a role that should not be his — King of Hell, World Rider, divinely-appointed weapon — and occupies it with the dissociated affect of a man waiting to be relieved of duty. Productivity drops within the role; he does the minimum required; he allows the apparatus around him to decay; he survives by reducing his interior presence in the position to the lowest setting that still registers. **This is Stage Five via dissociation rather than via violence**, and it is the morphology in which he is least dangerous to others and most dangerous to himself, because the long-running passive-suicidal accommodation that elsewhere expresses as recklessness expresses here as *absence*.

### Morphology V — *The Unmodulated Burn*

The rarest and worst. Triggered by combinations: Class D plus Class C, or Class B plus betrayal by an ally during the rescue. He goes from any stage to Stage Five via Stage Four in under an hour. Identity boundary with the Spirit collapses. Penance Stare is administered without proportion. Allies in the room are at non-zero risk. This morphology has occurred fewer than a handful of times in the recorded canon and has, in every case, required external intervention to terminate — Strange, Roxanne, the Simpson memory invoked directly, or in one case the involuntary exhaustion of the Spirit itself.

---

## 6.5 Recovery: What Has Worked, What Has Not

**What has worked, in descending order of reliability:**

1. **Proximity of a pre-curse attachment figure.** Roxanne, the Simpson family memory invoked directly, the surviving fragments of the carnival cohort. These reach the layer beneath the trauma. Reliability: high when available.
2. **A new innocent in need.** Counterintuitive but documented: redirecting his decompensation into Morphology III often resolves the immediate Stage Four or Five state by giving the surviving moral compass a target. Reliability: moderate; risk of stacking morphologies.
3. **Forced theological intervention.** Strange-grade or higher mystical containment, applied without his consent, has occasionally terminated Morphology V episodes. Reliability: moderate; cost to the relationship is high and he does not forgive it quickly.
4. **The road itself.** Returning him to movement, alone, under sky, on the bike, with no one watching, has resolved Morphology IV episodes by reactivating the version of him that exists between obligations. Reliability: moderate, slow, but cheap.
5. **Sleep, if achievable.** Almost never achievable in Stage Three or above without external intervention, but when achieved produces a one-stage downshift reliably.

**What has not worked:**

1. **Reasoning with him about the curse.** The damnation belief is load-bearing; arguments against it are processed as either naive or manipulative.
2. **Praise, esteem, validation, the offer of redemption.** See Class F. Counterproductive.
3. **Group therapeutic frames.** He will not speak in them. The Avengers basement period is the long-form demonstration.
4. **Pharmacological intervention.** His somatic substrate is not reliably the substrate of an ordinary nervous system; standard agents do not act predictably and the supernatural co-passenger metabolizes some of them.
5. **Confinement.** Class E stressor; produces decompensation rather than relieving it.
6. **The promise of futurity.** Plans involving him six months from now activate his belief that he will not be available, and he begins arranging his unavailability immediately.

---

## 6.6 The Floor He Has Not Yet Hit

The file would be incomplete without naming the failure mode he has, across six decades, **not** yet exhibited and which his profile suggests he is capable of. He has not, in any documented episode, **knowingly and lucidly turned the Spirit against an innocent**. The moral compass has survived every collapse morphology, including Morphology V. The structural risk in the profile — and the reason this file exists at this length — is that the load-bearing belief ("I am damned") and the load-bearing function ("I protect the helpless") are held together only by his refusal to integrate the rage as his own. **Should an event force integration** — should he be made, by circumstance or by an adversary's design, to accept authorship of the Spirit's worst administrations as his own — the prediction is not that he becomes a villain. The prediction is that the moral compass, encountering the integrated self, **convicts him**, and that the long-running passive-suicidal accommodation completes its sentence.

He has been, for fifty years, a man postponing the verdict he has already returned on himself. The failure mode he has not yet hit is the day he stops postponing.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT — SUBJECT: JOHN "JOHNNY" BLAZE

*Compiled as the terminal section of the standing dossier. The purpose here is not prediction in the oracular sense but the construction of a decision-tree: where the subject is, what vectors are loaded, which inflections are plausible across the next operational decade, and what — concretely — would push him along each branch. The subject is fifty-plus years into a stable pathology that has nevertheless preserved moral function; the question is not whether he will change but in which direction the slow drift will resolve when the next forcing event arrives.*

---

## 1. THE BASELINE VECTOR (no intervention)

If nothing external alters the trajectory, the subject's life continues on the line he has occupied for roughly five decades: itinerant, nocturnal, alcohol-anesthetized, geographically restless, episodically heroic, romantically isolated, theologically embittered, somatically punished. This is the **null-hypothesis future** and it is the most probable single outcome on any given five-year window because the subject is exceptionally well-adapted to its discomforts. He has metabolized loss into a habit; he has built infrastructure (the bike, the saddlebag economy, the cash-only motel circuit, the predator-detection heuristics) that supports indefinite continuation.

The null vector terminates in one of three ways:

1. **Attritional death in combat against a target he could have refused.** He goes into an engagement under-resourced, against an entity that exceeds even the Spirit's tolerances, on behalf of a stranger. He does not survive. He does not particularly try to survive. This is the modal endpoint and the one the canon has flirted with repeatedly without committing to.
2. **Reabsorption by Hell.** Mephisto, Blackheart, or a successor claimant successfully reasserts the original contract under altered conditions; Blaze ends as a permanent infernal asset. The Cates-era King-of-Hell tenure was a rehearsal for this.
3. **Stasis indefinitely prolonged.** He simply continues. Decades pass. He ages slowly or not at all (the canon is inconsistent; the curse appears to suppress ordinary senescence). He becomes a folkloric figure on the roads of the American interior — a man whose name truckers say at last call.

None of these are growth. All are stable equilibria around the existing pathology.

---

## 2. FORK POINTS — THE LOADED INFLECTIONS

There are a finite number of conditions under which the subject's organization could shift, in either direction. Each is a specific lever, with specific predictors of the direction of resolution.

### 2.1 The Reappearance of a Living Child Belonging to Him

The single highest-amplitude lever. The Aaron-era family was taken; the operational status of his son is variously rendered across continuity, and the subject treats the question as closed in the way trauma victims close questions they cannot tolerate reopening. **If a child of his — biological or functionally adopted — surfaces alive and in need of sustained, non-crisis parenting**, the entire defensive architecture is stressed at its load-bearing seam.

- **Growth branch.** He accepts the parenting role under a model he constructs deliberately *against* Crash Simpson's: presence over spectacle, ordinariness over rescue, the boring permanence he was denied. This would require him to disaggregate love from sacrifice — the single hardest cognitive move available to him. If he can do it for a child, he can subsequently do it for himself.
- **Catastrophe branch.** He fails. He attempts the role, transformations intrude, he constructs the same conditional-love structure he was raised inside, and the child experiences the same abandonment he experienced. He recognizes the recurrence. The resulting self-loathing closes the last door on integration. Probable behavioral output: withdrawal of unprecedented depth, escalation of drinking past the functional threshold, and willingness to accept the Mephisto reabsorption option as a form of self-removal from the child's life.

**Predictor of branch:** whether he permits a second adult (most plausibly Roxanne, if she is alive in current continuity; otherwise a peer such as Strange or Wanda or, less likely, his brother) to witness and correct his parenting in real time. Solo, he fails. Witnessed and corrected, he has a fighting chance.

### 2.2 A Sustained, Mutual, Non-Crisis Reunion with Roxanne Simpson

The Roxanne relationship has, in every era, been structured by crisis: she appears when he is in danger, or he appears when she is. They have never been depicted maintaining a quiet domestic week. **A reunion staged outside crisis** — chosen, not forced — is the second-highest-amplitude lever.

- **Growth branch.** The subject discovers that he can be in a room with her without something being on fire. He learns to sit. He learns that her presence does not have to be earned by rescue. The discovery is small and revolutionary. It generalizes slowly to other relationships.
- **Catastrophe branch.** He cannot tolerate the absence of structuring crisis. He manufactures crisis (picks fights, takes contracts that endanger her, transforms unnecessarily) until the relationship reverts to its familiar shape or terminates. She, having aged and accumulated her own clinical insight across decades, recognizes the manufacturing and leaves on her own terms. He registers this as confirmation of damnation.

**Predictor of branch:** whether he is willing to be bored in her company. Boredom is the diagnostic. If he can be bored with her, he can be loved by her. If he cannot, he cannot.

### 2.3 An Offered Severance from the Spirit That He Believes Is Genuine

He has been separated from Zarathos multiple times across continuity and has, each time, found his way back to the bond — sometimes by external force, sometimes by what reads as election. The next severance offer (and there will be one; the cosmology of his book produces them on a roughly decadal cadence) is a fork.

- **Growth branch.** He accepts the severance and *does not seek re-bonding when the next innocent is endangered.* He delegates. He learns the world contains other instruments. He becomes a man who used to be the Ghost Rider, and who is now something smaller and more sustainable — possibly a teacher of successors (Robbie Reyes, Alejandra, Ketch), possibly a private citizen.
- **Catastrophe branch.** He accepts the severance, encounters the first post-severance atrocity he cannot personally interdict without the Spirit, and re-bonds under conditions worse than the original contract because his bargaining position is weaker. The repetition compulsion completes another circuit; the externalization deepens; the next severance offer, if it comes, is refused on the grounds that it is a trick.

**Predictor of branch:** whether, during the severance window, he can sit with the existence of evil he is not personally addressing. This is the deepest test his psychology offers. The probability he passes it without sustained external support (Strange, a therapist-figure, a religious community he does not cynically reject) is low.

### 2.4 A Theological Reconciliation He Cannot Dismiss

The Aaron-era Zadkiel betrayal closed the door on Heaven for him. He distrusts divine claimants categorically. But the canon is structured such that the genuinely divine occasionally intervenes (the Caretaker lineage, the original Spirits of Vengeance taxonomy, the rare un-deceptive angel). **An encounter with a divine entity whose benevolence is unambiguous and whose request of him is small** — not "be our weapon," but "rest" — is a fork.

- **Growth branch.** He accepts the small request. He permits the possibility that not every divine actor is a fraud. This loosens the "I am damned" load-bearing belief by a few degrees, which is enough to permit the other forks to resolve favorably.
- **Catastrophe branch.** He refuses. He interprets benevolence as the most sophisticated deception yet attempted on him. The refusal is psychologically expensive; it requires him to dismiss evidence, which costs cognitive integrity. Subsequent paranoia generalizes. Trust with mortal allies erodes.

**Predictor of branch:** whether the entity makes any demand at all beyond rest. If there is a demand, he refuses. If there is genuinely no demand, he is destabilized in a productive direction.

### 2.5 The Brother

His relationship with Daniel Ketch is the unresolved sibling rivalry of a man who never got to be a child, played out at adult scale with cosmic stakes. Across continuity it has been antagonistic, allied, fraternal-in-flashes, and tactically cold. The next sustained Ketch encounter is a fork.

- **Growth branch.** He recognizes that his resentment of Ketch is the displaced resentment of his mother's disappearance and his father's death — that Ketch is being asked to pay debts owed by the dead. He apologizes. The apology is structurally similar to the apology he has spent fifty years owing himself. Practice on Ketch makes the self-apology thinkable.
- **Catastrophe branch.** The rivalry hardens into a custodial fight over the Spirits, the bloodline, the mantle. They become each other's adversaries by attrition. Both lose. The Spirits move to other hosts who lack the Blaze-Ketch operational competence; the human cost of the rivalry is measured in failed interventions elsewhere.

**Predictor of branch:** whether the subject can name Naomi Kale aloud in Ketch's presence without flinching. He cannot, currently. Whether he can in five years is an open question.

### 2.6 A Slow, Patient Mortal Witness

The clinically most powerful intervention available to the subject would be the sustained presence of a non-supernatural adult who knew his history in full and remained anyway, expecting nothing, asking nothing, not flinching at the transformation, not theologizing the curse. This is the figure he has not had — Roxanne came closest but the relationship is too overdetermined by shared trauma to function as witness.

- **Growth branch.** Such a person appears. He does not drive them off. Over years — not months — the witness's continued presence accumulates as counter-evidence to "I am damned and will be left." The belief weakens. He does not become happy; he becomes habitable.
- **Catastrophe branch.** Such a person appears and he drives them off, deliberately, with maximum cruelty, to confirm the prediction. He grieves the loss privately and forever. The cruelty itself becomes new evidence of damnation, completing the loop.

**Predictor of branch:** whether he has, by the time this figure appears, accumulated even one corrective experience along any of the other forks. The witness-fork is the *integrator*; it works best when other branches have softened the substrate. Cold, it almost always resolves catastrophically.

---

## 3. THE OPEN QUESTIONS

A surveillance file of this depth is obligated to enumerate what it does not know, because the unknowns are where the next decade's behavior will be decided.

1. **Does he, in private, believe he is good?** All evidence is consistent with a man who suspects he is good and works to suppress the suspicion because confirming it would require revising fifty years of self-organization. But the suspicion's strength is not measurable from outside. If it is strong, growth is one corrective experience away. If it is weak, growth requires a sequence.
2. **What is his actual relationship to the Penance Stare?** Does he experience administering it as duty, as satisfaction, as horror, as nothing? The canon does not clearly say and he does not clearly know. The answer would substantially refine the differential between hypertrophied conscience and a sadistic register he has projected onto the Spirit.
3. **Has he, ever, in any continuity, slept a full night without nightmare?** If yes, the conditions under which that occurred are operationally critical. If no, the sleep architecture is itself a target for intervention and the cognitive degradation from chronic deprivation must be factored into every other assessment.
4. **What does he do with money?** He has earned, lost, refused, and inherited substantial sums across eras. The disposition pattern would reveal whether his asceticism is principled, compulsive, or merely the absence of any imagined use. We do not know.
5. **Does he pray?** Privately, when unobserved, in fox-hole moments. The canon shows him cursing Heaven; it does not show him in unmonitored solitude. The answer would clarify the theological grievance's depth — whether it is a closed verdict or an active argument he is still having.
6. **What is the subjective experience of transformation?** Pain? Relief? Nothing? Each implies a different intervention. Relief would suggest the Rider is functioning as affect regulation and severance would be destabilizing rather than freeing.
7. **Could he, if asked, name three things he wants for himself?** This is the dossier's diagnostic question. A subject who can answer is recoverable. A subject who cannot is in a deeper place than the behavioral record alone reveals.

---

## 4. GROWTH CONDITIONS — WHAT WOULD ACTUALLY HELP

Specified concretely, in operational rather than aspirational terms:

- **A fixed address held for not less than eighteen months.** Movement is his core defense; interrupting it without removing the option (he must be free to leave; he simply must choose, daily, not to) is the precondition for everything else. The address must be modest, rural-edge, and contain a workshop. A garage is non-negotiable. The bike must be present.
- **One peer relationship maintained across that period without crisis-pretext.** Strange is the most plausible candidate among extant figures — old enough, strange enough, theologically literate enough to neither flinch nor proselytize. Wanda, with shared experience of being a weapon, is a secondary candidate. The relationship must include shared meals, not shared missions.
- **Reduction of alcohol intake to a measurable, declining curve.** Not abstinence imposed from outside (which would trigger reactance) but a private project he sets and tracks. The tracking is the intervention; the quantity is downstream.
- **A creative or craft practice unrelated to combat.** Engine work qualifies. Woodworking would qualify. Anything in which his hands produce a non-destructive outcome and the outcome accumulates. The asceticism has denied him this; reintroducing it would give the body a vocabulary other than punishment.
- **Sustained contact with one child he is not rescuing.** A nephew, a neighbor's kid, a student. The exposure must be low-stakes and recurrent. He needs to learn that children can be present without being endangered, which would interrupt the core repetition.
- **One conversation, in full, with someone qualified to hear it, in which he describes the bargain of *Spotlight* #5 from inside his fifteen-year-old self.** He has never, in any depicted continuity, done this. The bargain is the unprocessed kernel. Until it is spoken to a competent listener, the rest is symptom management.

---

## 5. CATASTROPHE CONDITIONS — WHAT WOULD BREAK HIM

Equally specified:

- **Loss of Roxanne in a manner he can attribute to his own choice.** Not the curse taking her — that he has metabolized — but a moment in which he, sober and aware, chose action A over her safety, and she died. This would close the redemption fork permanently.
- **Confirmation that his son's posthumous state involves suffering attributable to his bargain.** The Aaron-era cosmology contains this possibility. If made explicit, it would terminate the moral compass — not because he would become evil, but because he would lose the conviction that protecting the helpless means anything, since he failed to protect the most helpless person he was responsible for.
- **A second Zadkiel-grade betrayal by a divine actor he had begun to trust.** He has one of these in him. A second produces categorical refusal of all alliance and likely the kind of unilateral action against Heaven that ends with him as the antagonist of someone else's story.
- **Permanent severance from the Spirit imposed against his will at a moment when an innocent is suffering.** Forced helplessness is the original wound. Reproducing it at scale, with witnesses, would collapse the structure.
- **Institutionalization.** Any sustained confinement — Avengers tower as obligation rather than choice, Hell-throne as duty rather than refusal, prison, hospital — erodes him at a measurable rate. He must be able to leave. The leaving is the integrity.
- **A successor he trains who dies on a mission he sent them on.** This would reproduce the Crash bargain with himself in Mephisto's role. It would be unsurvivable in any meaningful sense.

---

## 6. THE MOST PROBABLE TEN-YEAR PATH

Synthesizing the above against base rates and the canon's demonstrated narrative gravity:

Within the next operational decade, the subject will almost certainly be pulled into one further cosmological conflict at the scale of *Damnation* or *Fear Itself* — the cadence of such events in his life is roughly one per six to eight years and he is overdue. He will perform reliably and at cost. He will lose someone, probably a peripheral ally, possibly a more central one. He will withdraw afterward to the roads for a period measured in months. He will be located, against his preference, by a younger Spirit-bearer requiring guidance, and will provide it grudgingly and well. He will refuse a romantic reconnection offered during this period and regret the refusal in private. He will drink at the rate he has always drunk. He will not see a clinician. He will not pray aloud. He will rescue, conservatively, between forty and eighty strangers in the period, most of whom will never learn his name. He will not die. He will not heal. He will continue.

This is the predicted path. It is not the only path. The forks above are real and several of them are, on current evidence, within one corrective experience of resolving favorably. The dossier's recommendation, if a dossier of this kind is permitted recommendations, is that the corrective experiences be quietly arranged — the rural address made available, the peer relationship suggested, the child placed nearby, the listener prepared — and that he be allowed to encounter them as though by accident, since he will refuse anything offered as intervention.

He has earned the chance to be habitable. He will not ask for it. Whether he is given it, against his stated preferences and consistent with his deepest unspoken wish, is the question this file, in the end, exists to pose.

*— UATU, terminal section, dossier closes here pending next material event.*
